After I completed for you, oh sons, this book, which is the last of the science of medicine with its complement, and I reached the end in it, from its explanations and declarations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this treatise which is a part of the operation, that is, surgery by hand.
Since the operation by hand has been neglected in our region and time, and has been completely abandoned; until perhaps its science has perished and its track has been cut off, and nothing of it remains except small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which have been altered by hands, and error and hesitation occurred to them, until its intentions were closed and its use was prolonged. It seemed to me that I should revive it with the composition of this Treatise concerning it, according to the method of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation, and that I should come with the forms of cauterization and the rest of the instruments of work, with the addition of declarations and the preparation of what is necessary.
The reason for which a good artisan of it with his hand is not found in our time, is: that the art of medicine is long, and its author ought to exercise himself beforehand in the science of anatomy, which Galen described, until he knows the functions of the members, and their forms, and their conjunction and separation, and has cognition of the bones, and nerves, and muscles, and their number, and their going out, and the pulses of the veins, and the quiet ones, and the places of their exits.
And because of that, Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with a work is little, and especially in the art of hand.
We have already spoken about this at the beginning of this book.
Since he who is not knowledgeable about what we said concerning anatomy, does not understand, and already falls into error, by which men are harmed: just as I have seen many of them, who boast about this science, and throw themselves into it without knowledge, and without experience.
What happened is that I saw a physician make an incision into a scrofulous aposteme on the neck of a woman and he cut certain arteries in the neck, from which the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead at his hands.
And I saw another physician who presumed to extract a stone from a man which had progressed in his bladder, and the stone was large. He therefore approached him, and extracted it with a fragment of the bladder. For which the man died on the third day.
And I indeed had already been called to extract it, and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the weak man that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was receiving a stipend from a certain Duke of our land because of medicine, and it happened to a black eunuch who was with him that he got a fracture in his leg near the heel, and the physician hastened with his ignorance, and pressed the fracture above the wound with poultices, and applied a tight bandage, and did not allow the wound an expiration.
Then he treated him according to his desires. Afterwards he left him for several days and instructed him not to undo the bandage, and it remained thus until his leg became an aposteme and his foot, and it reached a state of destruction.
I was therefore called to him, and I hastened to undo the bandage, and tranquility followed, and he was relieved from his pains.
Truly the corruption had already been confirmed in the limb, and I could not restrain it.
Then the corruption ceased to spread through the limb until he died.
And I saw another physician who perforated a cancerous aposteme, and it became an ulcer after some days, until the evil of it was increased with the lord of the patient.
What is, that when it is pure cancer from melancholic humor, then it is not suitable to be pierced with iron at all, unless it is in a member that can tolerate it, so that the whole of it can be cut off.
And because of that, O sons, it is necessary for you to know that the operation with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, an operation to which health is associated, and an operation in which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already stirred up in every place of this book, where the operation comes, in which there is terror and fear.
For it is necessary for you to beware of that, and dismiss it: so that the stupid ones do not find a way to speak and to discredit.
Receive therefore the measure with solicitude and protection, and your weak ones with facility and firmness, and use the better way, obtaining grace from God for salvation and praiseworthy succession: and dismiss terrible distresses of difficult healing: and lift your souls from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation enters into your faith and your commodity.
For it is more remaining to your glory, and more elevated in this world, and afterwards to your quantities.
For Galen has already said in certain of his warnings. Do not treat the evil disease: lest you be named bad doctors.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
The first Chapter.
On cauterization with fire and sharp medicine, the chapter, and ordered from head to foot, and forms of instruments, and iron tools of cauterization: and all that is necessary in the operation.
The second Chapter.
On cutting and piercing, bloodletting and puncture, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and similar things to that: and the whole chapter, ordered with forms of instruments.
The third chapter.
Of restoration and dislocation and the cure of torsion and similar things to it: chapters, arranged from head to foot, and forms of instruments.
But before I mention the operation with it, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of its cauterizations and its nuisances: and in which complexions they are exhibited.
I say therefore, that the discourse on the quality of cauterization and its nuisance is a discourse complex and subtle, of science and a hidden secret.
And many wise men have also spoken about it and disagreed on it: and for myself I am satisfied with few of their discourses, fearing prolixity.
I say therefore, that cauterization is suitable universally for every complexion, which is with matter and without matter: excepting two complexions, which are a hot complexion without matter and a dry complexion without matter.
In the hot and dry complexions with matter they disagree. For some have said that cauterization is suitable for them. And others have said the opposite of that, namely that cauterization is not suitable for an illness which is from heat and dryness: since the nature of fire is heat: and it is unsuitable, that a hot and dry illness be healed with something hot and dry.
And he who says the opposite of that said: that through cauterization healing is done in every hot and dry illness which occurs in the bodies of men: since when you compare the body of a man and its humidities to the complexion of fire, you find the body of a man to be cold.
And I say this through his speech: that from the experiment he has already shown me that several times.
However, it is not fitting that he should proceed with that, unless he has already been tested and practiced in the chapter of Cautery's final exercise, and has recognized the diversity of the complexions of men, and the disposition of their illnesses, and the causes of them, and the accidents of them, and the span of time of them.
From the remaining complexions, however, there is no fear regarding use: and especially in cold and moist illnesses. For all physicians have already agreed on these, and they do not disagree with the judgment of using Cautery for them.
And know this, my sons, that the secret of curing by Cautery with fire, and its goodness over Cautery with burning medicine is that the fire is simple, whose action does not penetrate except to the member which is cauterized: and it does not harm another member joined to it, except with a little harm.
The action of the burning medicine penetrates to that which extends from the members: and perhaps it makes happen in a member an illness difficult to heal, and perhaps it kills.
The fire, however, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that, unless it overflows.
Now, however, that has become known to us through experiment, because of the length of service and study with art, and staying on the truth of things: and because of that I will excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not so, because it is not permitted to this book of mine, I would tell you a secret occult in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies of expelling, which expels illnesses, explained by philosophical speech, which would be sharpened in your minds.
And you should know what they themselves disagree about at the time when a cauterization is to be made, and they put on a better time for the chest.
And I say that a cauterization is suitable at every time, because the harm that occurs on account of the time is submerged in the benefit that is attracted with the cauterization. And especially if the cauterization is on account of necessary pains and strong, violent pains, which do not tolerate delay: because there is fear of a greater evil happening from them, than the small harm that occurs on account of time.
And do not let it fall into your minds, O sons, that which only the common and foolish physicians think, namely that for the ailment which is healed by a cauterization, there is not always a relapse: and they put that as a consequence, and the thing is not as they suppose: because the cauterization is not, except in place of medicine, which alters the complexion, and evacuates the humors which are the causes, from which the pains happen.
Truly, however, the cauterization surpasses medicine by the speed of its health, and the virtue of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion: and it is possible that the ailment returns at some hour of time according to the complexion of the infirm, and the location of its ailment, and its virtue: and what is prepared in his body from an aggregation of superfluities in it: and what pervades to it in its acquisition from foods, and similar things from causes, unless the ailment is made, in which the cauterization is administered.
A subtle ailment in a member with few superfluities and humors, such as the cauterization of a tooth, on account of pain, and similar things to it, it is possible that the pain does not return in it. But that suits few.
And the common speech of the people is that cauterization is the last resource of medicine, which is a true speech, not for that which they themselves intend in it: since they believe that there is no cure which agrees with medicine, nor with anything else after the application of the cauter.
But the thing is contrary to this, and the intention that cauterization is the last resource of medicine is not so, except that when we administer methods of cure in some diseases, and those medicines do not work: then we administer cauterization at the end, and it works: thence it follows that cauterization is the last resource of medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron: and they did not say this except because of the equality of gold, and the loftiness of its substance: and they said that it does not produce pus in the place of the cauter. But it is not true absolutely: since I have already proven that, and found that it does not do so in certain bodies without others.
And cauterization with gold is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However when you make a cauter of gold in the fire, it is not shown to you when it is ignited according to the quantity that you need, because of the redness of the gold: and when it attains its full heat, and if you add ignition on top of it, it melts in the fire and turns into plates.
Wherefore the artisan fails from that in his work: and because of this iron cauter is made by us more quickly and nearer to perfection for the operation.
And I have already arranged this Chapter on Cauterization, according to the chapters: and arranged them from head to foot: so that they may alleviate whoever seeks what he wants from it.
Head II
This cauterization is beneficial for dominating humidity and coldness above the brain: which two are the causes of numbness, and the multitude of flux of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and the multitude of sleep, and toothache, and throat ache: and universally all illness that occurs from coldness, such as paralysis, and numbness, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar to those illnesses.
The method of cauterization is that you should first prepare the weak: so that it may be evacuated in the beginning with a medicine that cleanses and purifies the head for three nights, or four, according to what the strength of the weak person demands, and their age, and their habit.
Then command them to shave their head with a razor. Then make them sit between your hands, with their hands placed on their chest, so that they have already put their hands on their breast.
Then put the root of your palm on the root of their nose between their eyes. Wherever your middle finger touches, mark that place with an incision or branding iron.
Then prepare the cauterization of olive oil: whose form is this.
Then put it on the marked place with the incision, while your hand contracts slowly, and you turn it. Then lift your hand quickly, and inspect the place.
If you see that it has already drawn out from the bone a quantity of head alkali, or a quantity of theriac, then lift your hand. And if not, return your hand with the iron itself, or with another one by itself if it cools: until you see the bones that I told you.
Then take something from salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the cotton in it, and apply it to the place; and leave it for three days.
Then apply over it cotton soaked in butter, and leave it on the place until the eschar is destroyed by fire. Then treat it with the ointment tetrapharmacon, until it is healed.
For they have said that the more a wound remains open, the more it emits pus, which is better and of greater benefit.
And some of them have said that the skin should be cauterized up to the bone, and that the cauterization should be applied until it reaches something of the thickness of bone.
Then scrape away what has been burned from the bone, then treat it.
And others say that it is necessary to pierce through with a cauterization iron to the extreme, until it impresses on the bone an impression of a fetid smell, so that the bone falls away, which is formed like a crater: or an instrument that women put in the infusion of the alphabet of the puerperal: and they extract, what they exhale from this place vapors of the head, and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then let it be treated, until it becomes consolidated.
To me, however, these two types of cauterization do not seem suitable except in certain men according to the way of fear.
And leaving it alone is better for me with its own health.
For the head is weakened from the solution of its natural continuity: as we have testified in the other members: and especially when the head is weak by nature: and a certain species of Cauterization is more salutary and better for me, and I use it: therefore I operate with it for health.
Chapter Three.
When a chronic pain occurs in the whole head, and it is prolonged in the weak person, and it is treated with henna, and cichorium, and head purges, and oils, and plasters. And especially if it has already been cauterized with a single cauterization that we have described, and none of those things are of benefit to it: then consider. For if the head of the weak person is of strong natural creation, and it is not feeble, and it finds intense cold: then cauterize with another cauterizer under that a little. Then cauterize it itself over every horn of its head with a cauterizer, so that the skin is not pierced, and a quantity is discovered from the bone, which we have described. And cauterize it itself with a single cauterizer on the back of its head, in the place that is called "uas", and it is the place where the ventouse is put: and raise your target in this, and do not discover the bone. For the weak person finds relief because of that vehement pain, and it is different from the pain of the other cauterizations of the whole head.
And I will say that this cauterization is in its own place: and it is necessary that it be a cauterizer, with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and its occiput more subtly than the cauterizer with which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter Four.
When pain and swelling occur in a part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and it is treated with medicines that cleanse the head, and the rest of the treatment that I mentioned in the divisions of diseases is administered, and none of those things are of benefit: then cauterization in this case is according to two methods: either cauterization with medicine burnt by fire, or with iron.
Cauterization with a sharp caustic medicine is such that you take one tooth of a badger, and scrape it, and cut off its extremities on both sides. Then cut the place of pain at the time with a broad lancet, until a place is made under the skin, in which the dens is captured.
Insert it therefore under the skin, until it is hidden: then bind over it with a bandage of decent constriction, and leave it for fifteen hours; then untie it, and extract the badger, and leave the wound two days, or three; afterwards put on it a plaster submerged in butter, until the place makes pus: then cure it with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you want to make it with certain sharp medicines, which I wrote about in the twelfth treatise, on caustic medicines.
Cauterization of it with iron is according to this method. Fire cauterization, whose form is this.
And it is named a Clavulus: because the form of its head is like the form of a nail, in which there is something curved, and in the middle of it is a certain small prominence.
Then put it on the place, and hold your hand: and you withdraw the iron little by little with swiftness: and let the quantity that is cauterized be from the thickness of the skin, as its middle. And lift your hand, so that the artery which is below is not cauterized, and there occurs a flow of blood.
Then soak the plaster in salt water, and put it on the place, and leave it for three days: then put a plaster with butter: afterwards cure it with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you want, cauterize this half of the skull with the edge of a second cauterizing knife. And beware of the incision of an artery in this half of the skull, not formerly its own.
On the method of cauterizing in old hemicrania.
When you treat hemicrania, with what we said from the preceding cure, and what we said in the divisions of diseases, and the treatment does not work: and you see from the disease that what we said from the first cauterization with medicine, or with cauterization with fire is not enough for it, then it is necessary to make a burning cauterization, until it becomes white after you apply a sign above the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or about that: and put your hand in place of one, and press it until you cut an artery, and penetrate up to the bone.
Truly it is necessary for you to beware of the continuity of the jawbone, which moves during mastication, lest the side or nerve that moves it be burned, whence spasms happen.
And this is above caution, and warning about the flow of blood from an artery which has been cut. For in the cutting of it there is fear, and especially for him who does not know what he is doing, and is not diligent, nor experienced: and he gives up the operation with that at the beginning.
And I come with a reminder of the management of the flow of blood which happens from an artery according to its mode, and in the proper place of this book.
What if you see from the disease that this cauterization is not enough for it, and you see the weak body tolerating a cauterization on the middle of the head, as we have narrated, treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you use it, administer the cauterization that we said in the chapter on the extraction of an artery with a cauterizer having two knives. For cauterization is better than this and more beneficial.
On the method of cauterizing in ear pain.
When pain occurs in the ear from cold, and it is treated with solutions, and the rest of the treatment that we mentioned in the division, and the pain is not relieved, then cauterization by fire: and this is what is called a point, whose shape is this.
Then puncture with it after its ignition around the entire ear, as it revolves: or around both, if pain is in both. And stretch yourself with the cauterizing instrument from the root of the ear for a short while, after you have marked the place with ink, and let the quantity of cauterization be ten punctures on all the ear, or thereabouts.
Then treat the places until they heal.
On the method of cauterizing for Twisting.
Chapter Seven.
Twisting that is treated with cauterization, is not unless from species which occur from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of diseases.
And it demands cauterization of the species that occurs from dryness and nerve spasm.
When you treat this species of twisting with hienas, and head purges, and gargles, and your treatment does not work, then it is necessary to cauterize the weak place with three cauterizations: one at the root of the ear, and a second a little below its temple, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And put your cauterization on the opposite side of the weak part. For softening does not occur, except in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with the cauterizing instrument at the top extremity of the ear, a little below the horn of the head, and another on the temple: whose length is according to the length of the thumb. And put your hand with the cautery until the quantity of the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the Cautery, and it is a species from a knife, whose form is previously described: nevertheless it is not more subtle than that little, as you see: and it should be a knife with a bit of superfluous thickness.
Then heal the place, with what has preceded, until it is cured.
On the method of cauterizing in old Apoplexy.
When the Apoplexy has become old and you treat it with what we have said, and your medication is not effective, and the weak person does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on every horn of his head, and a cauterization in the middle of the head, as we have said, and a cauterization on the back of the head, according to what has preceded: and the method of the cauterization should be according to what has preceded.
And it is also cauterized with a Cautery over the bone of the stomach: and this is more extreme.
Then let it be cured, with what has preceded.
Chapter 9.
It is necessary that at first the weak person should be given to drink great draughts, and cleansing pills for the brain.
Then shave the entire head of the weak person, and put on its back a plaster of the snail described in the treatise on plasters: and apply it several times.
This indeed is the method of the Cautery: and do that according to the same order which I have mentioned there.
If therefore he is cured by it, it is good. If not: then make for him three cauteries on the back part of his head, which extend from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye: and put between each cauterization the thickness of a finger.
Then treat the cauterization, with what has preceded.
If indeed you use an application, and he is weak and cannot tolerate it: then apply a cauterization in the middle. What if you use an application: then cauterize it over the two horns.
Then treat it, until it is healed: and let the cauterization be according to the form that has been described beforehand.
On the method of cauterizing for paralysis and softening.
Chapter 10.
It is fitting that you proceed with the cleansing of the head with care, and with what we have said.
Then shave the head of the weak person: afterwards cauterize it with a cauterization in the middle of the head, and with a cauterization over every horn of the head, and with a cauterization over its back, and with three on the vertebrae of the neck.
If indeed you immerse in the disease of softening of the body many of them, and he is weak and cannot tolerate it, and the disease is strong: then cauterize it with four cauterizations on the vertebrae of the back, and the last one with a cauterization, until it is greatly burned from its skin, and lift your hand. Then treat it, until it is healed: and thus the cauterization of olive oil.
On the method of cauterizing for epilepsy.
The epileptic is not cauterized, unless it is one whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
It is necessary therefore that you cleanse his brain first with care, and with the rest of the treatment which we have spoken of in division: when the weak person is great, or is tolerant of the reception of medicines.
If indeed he is a boy, who does not tolerate medicines, then administer a gargle, and cleansing mastics for the brain, before that for many days with a strengthening of foods.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize it with one cauterization in the middle of the head, according to what has preceded in manner: and cauterize another on his occiput, and over every horn of his head with a cauterization. What if he is weak and unable to tolerate, then cauterize him with the cauterizations that I mentioned in one having palsy, and softening of the body on the spondiles of the neck, and the spondiles of the back: and let the cauterization be olive oil according to the method which has preceded.
If however he is a weak child, then apply a subtle cauterization, according to this method.
On the method of cauterizing in Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupt humors and gross phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauterizations that we mentioned in one having palsy.
And if the cause of melancholy is a surplus of declivity to melancholy, and the body of the weak is moist, then give him in drink what will cleanse his brain, according to that which has preceded in division: then shave the head of the weak, and afterwards make a tortella skillfully made from linen, like a circle.
Then put it on the middle of the head: and let the weak person sitting squarely be held from every side.
Then apply an ointment. And it is worthy made from old butter. And heat it over a fire with tempered heating to a measure that the finger can tolerate, when it is inserted into it. Then apply it on the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools.
Do that to the weak person once a week, with the rest of his good regimen, until he is cured.
Or if you use it, apply a cautery to it making many small points, besides which you should hold the hand with the cautery and smell it.
This type of cautery moistens the brain with a quality.
Then put on top of it a cotton pad soaked in butter or hen's fat.
On the method of applying a cautery to the descending water of the eye.
Chapter 13.
When the beginning of the water in the eye is declared to you by signs, which I mentioned in the division, then begin and drink the weak one, with what purifies its head.
And guard it from all moistures, and make it sit in a bath, in fasting for some days.
Then command it to shave its head, and apply a cautery to the middle of its head. Then apply a cautery to it on the two temples with two cauteries, if there is a descending water in both eyes at the same time: or from one side, if there is a water in one eye: and cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long across the width of the temples: and beware of the flow of blood.
What if you see anything of it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of the arteries, and cutting them, and caution from the flow of blood.
And sometimes a cautery is applied to the neck, under the two bones, with two cauteries produced from the back.
On the method of applying a cautery to old tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and constant: and they are above the veins and arteries which are in the manifest head exteriorly, it is verified that this is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities: then apply a cautery with the same cautery that I narrated for the descending water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries in the neck under the two bones. And if you notice an increase, then cauterize it on every side with a cautious eye, above the eyebrow with a small cauterizer.
On the method of cauterizing in the nostrils.
When you treat it with what we have said in the division and the treatment is not effective then hasten and give in drink a weak potion for three nights then shave his head and cauterize it with a moderate cauterizer with an olive oil cauterizer. Then cauterize it with a clamp-like cauterizer, with two cauterizers, above the two eyebrows under the hair a little.
And beware of the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the clamp-like cauterizer.
On the method of cauterizing for softening of the Eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by disease or moisture then cauterize the eyelid with one cauterizer, with this crescent-shaped cauterizer.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauterizers on every side and they will stretch out from both temples and let the length of every cauterizer be according to the lengths of the eyebrow and do not extend your hand with the cauterizer, but according to the quantity that is burned by the third eyelid.
On the method of cauterizing the eyelid when inverted lashes prick the eye.
The cauterization is according to two methods: either cauterization with fire or cauterization with burning medicine.
With the fire cauterizer, however, instruct the weak one beforehand, that he let his eyelashes fall out, if he is one of those who clean them, until they become longer and even. If they then prick him at his own throat: then bind his eyes with a cloth, so that they do not move, until they are healed.
When therefore the ulcers have formed and levelled, then put the head of the weak person in your bosom: afterwards mark over the eyelid of his eyes with a caustic, a mark which is according to the shape of myrtle leaves: and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then put a cloth dipped in vinegar on the white of the eye: or in a mucilage of psyllium over the eye.
Then apply a cautery, whose shape is this.
Then cauterize over the figure that you marked little by little on many a vein, until the surface of the skin is burned, which is like the shape of myrtle leaves, appearing wholly proper.
And the sign of the health of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted, and hairs elevated at the puncture of the eye.
Lift your hand then: and leave it for three days.
Then put over it a cloth with butter, until the scab is eradicated. Then treat it with an ointment, until it is healed.
Which if some of the hairs return after an hour, and the eyelid becomes soft: then apply a cautery again over that place, as you did at first.
If however the hairs are on the underside: then cauterize it, until they are elevated to their natural place: and are evened so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is that you advise the weak person to leave the hairs alone, until they grow out and are evened. Make from a piece of cloth the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap, and from non-absorbed lime one ounce or about that; then rub those together with good friction, and make it with haste, so that it does not get cold. Then spread from the paste over the cloth which you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and put it on the eyelid of one eye or two. And put under the eye a small piece moistened with egg white: and let the head of the weak person be on your lap.
And put your index finger on the medicine, and press it gently for a little while. And you should move it as often as the weak person feels the biting of the medicine: for its biting penetrates like fire.
While therefore it persists, what it itself has found, the biting, then remove the medicine, and move it with your finger. When therefore the biting has ceased, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And consider then, if you see the eyelid lifted, as it is lifted with contraction from fire, or with incision, it is good: and if not, then apply again on it medicine on the place where the medicine does not press and does not blacken, until your operation is equal, and the eye is contracted.
Then put over it a small piece with butter, until the skin of the burn is peeled off. Then treat it with ointment called diaphenicum, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you during the operation to guard with utmost care, lest something from the medicine falls into the eye.
What if the eyelid becomes soft after some days, and something from the hair strikes against the eye, then apply again medicine on that place which becomes soft from the eyelid itself, as you did at first. Then treat it, until it heals.
And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And you should know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness. Therefore your consideration should be according to that, and the way of correctness will not be hidden from him who has a desire for this art.
On the method of cauterizing in the tear duct.
When you treat a fistula, with what we have said regarding the divisions of diseases, and your treatment does not work, then it is necessary to cauterize it according to this method.
Order the weak person to place his head on your lap, and let your assistant hold his head between his hands in such a way that it is not moved or shaken with his head.
Then put a cushion underneath in the white of the eye or in the mucus of the psil on the eye of him, then ignite the cauterization instrument whose shape is this.
Let it be hollow, like the shape of a quill pen from one end, with which cauterization is done, and if you want it to penetrate to the other end, and if you want it raised thus.
However, this hollow one is better for your work.
Then express the fistula, if it is open, and extract from it the sanies, and cleanse it, and if it is not open, then open it, and extract its pus.
Then put on it the cauterization instrument, which is made ignited strongly.
And hold your hand for a short time with the cauterization instrument near the eye, towards the nose, so that your hand is not tremulous, nor the weak person disturbed, and you put the cauterization instrument in the fat of the eye, and destroy it.
If I perforate at the beginning of your cauterization up to the mouth, it will be good. And if not: then repeat the cauterization once or twice, if you need it: and leave it for three days.
Then put a plug with butter, and treat it with excitatory ointment, until it is healed.
What if forty days pass and it is not healed: then put on it a sharp corroding medicine, until the mouth is revealed: and shave it according to what is described in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some of the first ones have described. Direct to the place of the fistula and find it: then put into its fissure a thin canula, that is, a subtle little reed, whose shape is this. And pour into it a quantity of drachm of melted lead, and hold your hand with the cane in good retention, and let not the weak one move at all, so that the melted lead does not run or perforate to its eye.
And it is necessary that you put on the weak eye a plug under the white of the eye, or in water.
For lead burns the place of the fistula and heals it with a wonderful healing.
What if the fistula is healed, with what we have said concerning cauterization and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the nasal passage, and reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what will come in its proper place.
On the method of cauterizing in the fissures of the lips.
Many times there occur in the lip fissures, which are called Pili, and especially in the lips of children.
When you treat their fissures, with what we have said in the division of ailments, and the treatment does not work, then apply a small cautery to the knife, according to this method.
And let it be sharpened according to the fineness of the knife.
Then put the ignited thing quickly into the same fissures, until the cautery penetrates to the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with a dressing, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing a fistula of the mouth.
When a boil occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth: then it makes pus, and bursts: afterwards it becomes chronic, and the pus runs, and a fistula is formed: then you treat it, and if the treatment does not work, then it is necessary to apply a cautery according to the quantity that the fistula can contain. Then insert the ignited thing into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand, until the ignited iron penetrates to its depth and end: do this once, or two times.
Then treat it afterwards, with what we have said concerning treatment, until it is cured.
If the pus is then cut off, and healed, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to probe the place, and remove the corrupted bone according to what is found in its head.
On the method of cauterizing the gum and softening teeth.
When the gum becomes softened because of humidity, and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines, and it does not work: then put the head of the weak one on your lap.
Then apply a cautery, whose form will be described after this, so that you put a tube over the tooth: and insert into it the ignited cautery quickly: and hold your hand for a little while, until the weak one feels the heat of the fire has already penetrated to the root of the tooth.
And raise your hand: then repeat the cauterization several times, according to what you need.
Then let the weak bone fill itself with salt water, and hold it for one hour: and spit it out.
For a dense movement is strengthened, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted humidity is dried.
On the method of cauterizing in toothache.
When the toothache is due to cold, or there is cold or worm in it, and treatment with medicines is not effective: then cauterization on it is according to two methods: either cauterization with butter, or cauterization with fire.
The cauterization of it with butter is, that you take cow's butter, and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a pan. Then take the scum, and apply it to the extremity of the affected tooth. Then dip it into the boiling butter: and put it quickly on the aching tooth, and hold it until it cools: then repeat it several times, until the power of the fire penetrates to the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, dip a thread, or scum into cold butter, and put it on the painful tooth: and place over it a heated iron, until the fire penetrates to the deep part of the hollow tooth.
The cauterization of it with fire is, that you apply to a bronze or iron tube. And let there be in its body something of thickness, so that the sharpness of the fire does not penetrate to the weak tooth.
Then apply the fire cauterization, which shape comes: and put it on that tooth: and hold your hand, until the cauterization cools.
Do this several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day, or on another day.
And it is suitable in the application of that cauterization, that it should fill the weak bone with good pus, and hold it for one hour; then it will spit it out.
And this is the form of the cauterization.
Cauterize with whatever extremity you use, according to what is possible: and this is the form of the Cannula.
On the method of cauterizing in Strictures.
When the Strictures are from phlegm and from cold humidities, and they do not obey digestion by means of medicines, and you wish to hasten their digestion: then apply a concave cauterization of fire, whose form is this.
Having two open extremities, so that the smoke can exit from the cauterization at the other extremity: and put the ignited thing over the aposteme once, and a second time, if you need it, until it penetrates to the depth of the aposteme.
Which if the aposteme is small: then put the cauterization according to the quantity of the aposteme.
Then leave it for three days, and put on top of it a plaster made with butter, until the burnt material is removed by the fire.
Then treat it with toothpaste ointment, until it heals in the form of a tube.
On the method of cauterizing for roughness of the voice and constriction of breathing.
When the humidities descend upon the canal of the lung, and especially when it is with a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the weak one should first be treated with soluble medicines.
Then cauterize it in the Adam's apple at the root of the throat in a depressed place: and beware, lest you penetrate with the cauterization to the throat, nor into the skin, except for a little of it.
Then cauterize it with a cautery at the joint of the neck in the last vertebra, and let the cautery be according to the method which has preceded.
Then treat it with what has preceded, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for diseases of the Lung and Cough.
When cough and disease of the lung are from cold humidities, and the weak person has no fever, nor consumption, and not an old disease: then cauterize it with two cauteries above the fork in depressed, gentle, empty places. And cauterize with another on the middle of the chest between the two breasts: and let the cautery be of a tube according to the form which has preceded.
And if you need to cauterize by pricking with a cautery, which is called a Point, whose form has preceded in the pricking of ear pain: and let the points be from thirty points up to almost a hundred.
Then treat it with what has preceded, until it is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this form. For it will be lightened with that cautery, when you make with it one of three cauteries.
Chapter 27.
When the head of the arm is dislocated due to a cause of humidities, and it does not return to its place in the hour of its return from its dislocation, until it becomes accustomed to returning, then it dislocates from a slight movement, which happens as we have already shown, then it is necessary that you reduce the dislocation first. Then let the weak person lie on his back, or on his healthy side. Then elevate the cut which is inside the inner thigh to the upper parts with the fingers of your left hand and if the joint becomes dislocated inwardly.
Then apply cauterization to it with two irons. Its shape is this.
Then cauterize the cut until it penetrates to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization comes with four cauterizations.
And when the cauterization is made with a cauterizer having three irons, then the figure of the cauterization is made with six cauterizations and they are irons according to the subtlety of the sensation.
And this is the shape of the cauterizer having three irons.
And when one is added in this manner, then there are eight cauterizations.
Then put on the cauterization ground pork with salt. Then apply a dressing to the wound for tranquility, so that it is not moved for some time, until it becomes strong.
And if the dislocation is upward and it rarely happens, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a cauterizer for the shoulder or with many punctures.
For the joint is strengthened, and the moisture is removed, and the weakness is healed.
On the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When there occur in the stomach many colds and humidities, until they extract it from its combination, and multiply the catarrhs to it, and assiduous methods of cure, and do not strengthen: then it is necessary that the weak person lies on his back, and stretches out his legs, and hands. Then cauterize with three cauterizations, one cauterizer under the shoulder of the chest the size of one finger, with a shoulder cauterizer, and two cauterizations below by the two sides of one cauterizer, until the figure of the cauterizations comes in a triangle. And let it stretch between both so that they do not join, when they make pus.
And let the depth of the cauterization be a quantity of two thirds of the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of the cauterizations be according to this form without addition, and if you want to cauterize with a large cauterizer in the middle of the stomach according to this form, and let the cauterization that is made be one according to the figure of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking him who trembles from this cauterization: and it is, that you mark on the stomach a point according to the quantity, which you want with the encaustic, then cauterize it with the cauterizer of the point: then cure it with the treatment, which preceded until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing a cold liver.
When there occurs in the liver pain from cold and moisture, or from a thick flatulence, until it goes out from its natural passage, and the weak person is cured with what we have said, and it does not benefit him: then it is necessary that the weak person be placed on his back, and marked with encaustic three cauterizations according to this figure, and of the same quantity on the lower liver below the hypocondriac region, where the elbow of the man reaches: and let the space that is between each cauterization be according to the thickness of a finger: and let the cauterization be according to the length of the body straight: and do not press your hand much with the cauterizer.
And let the quantity of what is cauterized be from the thickness of the skin, the quantity of half of it not added: and let the weak person stand on his feet.
If however he is not standing, then let him be lying, who has already extended his legs and lifted his arms.
This is the form of a cautery.
And it is possible for you to cauterize these cauterizations with a knife cautery, when there is subtlety and prudence in the art.
And beware, lest you proceed to the utmost in cauterization, and the thickness of the whole skin is burned, where the whole body is burned, and it penetrates to the intestines: for the skin there is subtle, therefore know that.
On the method of cauterizing apostems of the liver.
When there is a flow of matter, and you want to know if that apostem is in the flesh of the liver or in its tunic: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, a weak pain and heaviness come on without sharpness: and if it is in the tunic of the liver, with pain there is vehement sharpness: and you see already, which has wearied the physicians with its cure.
It is necessary therefore that the weak man breathes upon his neck. Then figure the place of the apostem with a searing cautery: then ignite a cautery that is similar to a radius. And this is its form. And cauterize with it one cautery, until the whole skin is burned, and it penetrates to the siphac, until all the sanies come out: then cure it with the cure of flowing ulcers, until it is healed.
And it is not necessary that this species of cautery be used, except by one whose study in the art of medicine is prolonged: and through whose hands these diseases run with experiment many times: then therefore he dares to undertake an operation of this kind.
But to omit it, is better in my opinion.
On the method of cauterizing in the Pleura.
The ancients said, a cautery with the roots of aristolochia for a cold Pleurisy in this manner. And it is, that you take from the roots of the dry long aristolochia, one root which is longer, that is found on it, and let it be the size of a finger. Then submerge it in oil: and set it on fire. Then cauterize with one cautery at what is between the junction of the jaw and the neck, and with two small cauteries under the guidance of a little declining towards the part that is under the beard.
And also with two cauteries at what is between the fifth and sixth ribs, declining towards the back a little: and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries at the back: one at what is between the two shoulder blades: and with two cauteries on the two sides of the chest, below the cautery that is between the two shoulder blades.
And it is not necessary that you press your hand with the cautery, but rather that it be on the manifest skin smelling.
And some of the ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery made of iron like a probe: and they ignite it, and insert it inside between the ribs, until they reach with it to the same abscess, and the pus comes out: as we have said in the chapter on Abscesses.
But in this perforation with the cautery there is fear that either the weak person dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, for which there is no healing.
On the method of cauterizing the Spleen Chapter XXXII.
When you treat an illness of the spleen, with what we have said about curation in the division of illnesses, and your treatment is not effective, then a cautery on it is according to three methods, all of which are correct.
Of which one is, that you make three or four cauteries in a line along the length of the spleen according to the figure of the cauteries of Epatus, whose figure has preceded.
And let there be between the cauterization a quantity of the thickness of a finger, or a little more.
And let the method of cauterization be that which we have mentioned in the cauterization of the liver equally.
And do not press your hand with the cauterizer, and let the patient lean weakly on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: as we have said in the chapter on the dislocation of the shoulder, that there are two cauteries for the ignias, and raise the skin which is in line with the spleen, where the weak left elbow meets: and let your elevation be such that you elevate the skin according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert two ignited cauteries by force, until you penetrate the skin from the other side: then withdraw the cauterizer: thus four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cauterizer having three rods.
Then take care that the cauterization, after you apply it, discharges pus for many days: for it is more beneficial than all the rest that have preceded in the cure.
Of the method of cauterizing in Dropsy.
The cauterization does not fall into Dropsy, except for the hardened ascleros.
When you treat a dropsical person with the methods of cure which we have mentioned in the division, and the cure is not effective, then it is necessary that you cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and one cauterizer on the stomach, and another cauterizer on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two cauteries behind the back between the shoulders, and one in line with the breast, and another in line with the stomach: and let the quantity of the depth of the cauterization be near to the thickness of the skin.
Then diminish the open cauterization so that it emits pus over a long period.
And it does not evacuate the weak from cure after cauterization with it, for which two intentions are required to be added to it: and the healing will hasten with the aid of God.
The form of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized, should be a clamp, according to the form that preceded it: and that with which the back is cauterized, should be an olive, according to the form that preceded it.
On the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When there are apostemations on a hydropic patient, and they are filled with citrine water: it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot in the nocturnal, which is between the ear and the ring finger: and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it: then raise your hand: and do not repeat it at all.
For the citrine water will flow out, and let the cautery be according to this form.
Then make on the two legs two cauteries, one on each leg, and let the cautery be made with the extremity of a knife-shaped cautery: and let the cautery be made according to the length of the leg, one below the knee, and another lower than that, around the middle of the leg: and on every hip make two cauteries: and diminish the open cautery without cure for a long time: so that some water flows out from it: then cure it with the remaining things that we have said.
On the method of cauterizing for the relief of the belly.
Chapter 35.
When there is a solution of the belly from cold and humidities, until it debilitates the retaining and digesting virtues, which are in the stomach and intestines: and it is cured with modes of cure, and not healed: and you see the weak tolerating the cautery of exuberant virtue, then cauterize it with a great cautery on its stomach, according to what preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with a ring-shaped cautery, and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle clamp-shaped cautery: and a great cautery above the hips, or two cauteries.
And if you see excessive moistures and the weak tolerance of that, then cauterize it with a cauterizing iron on the chest, and cauterize all of it with a cauterizing iron: and perhaps you will add two small cauterizations on the stomach near the large one.
It is indeed a profitable treatment, whose benefit does not fail.
On the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter 36.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus, or one, and they are from gross, cold, or corrupt humors, and they are treated with what we said in the division, and the treatment is not effective: then cauterize with three cauterizations above the lower vertebra of the back under the almeidati for a short time in a triangular fashion, and cauterize under the navel almost two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face breaking out in pimples, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cauterizing iron, according to what came before: and cauterize on his liver, and another on his spleen, with a cauterizing iron on the hip: and leave the cauterized place open for some time: then treat him until he is cured.
Chapter 37.
When you excise the tonsils, then ignite a cauterizing iron that resembles a staff. Then insert the ignited iron into the excised tonsil: and with your last hand, until the cauterizing iron reaches the opening of the vein, from which blood runs: do that once, or twice.
If therefore there are many tonsils, then cauterize each one with a cauterizing iron according to what we have narrated. Then treat them with what constricts them from ointments until they are healed.
And if you cauterize it with a large cauterization on the alcatin, it is the greatest in treatment of the injury.
On the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter 38.
When the weak one does not undergo the operation and treatment that we described in its own place, and is deterred by it, perhaps it will be healed with a cauterization.
When therefore a fistula occurs to someone, and it becomes chronic, corrupt pus runs out of it, and rotten moistures. It is more worthy therefore that which ought to be, that you should probe it with a subtle sound. Then know the quantity of its depth with the probe.
Then apply a cauterization iron, which is similar to a probe. Then insert the ignited instrument itself into the same fistula and the quantity in which the nail entered.
And repeat over it the cauterization, until all those rotten bodies are burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to the quantity of your necessity.
And beware of the burning of the nerve, if it is there, or of the large vein: or if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then beware of all these places.
And do not do that, unless when the fistula is in a fleshy place: and you think that it is not penetrating.
Then treat the place until it is healed.
If however the place is closed, and matter is cut off from it, and it remains thus for a long time: then know that it is already healed completely.
And if matter is not cut off from it, then know that it is penetrating, or in its depth there is a rotten mouth, or something like that: whose reminder will come into its own place.
On the method of cauterizing the kidney.
When pain occurs in the kidneys due to cold or gross flatulence and it weakens because of that, then it is necessary to cauterize it on the alumethen over the kidneys, with a cauterizing iron over each kidney, using an iron clamp, whose description has preceded.
And perhaps we will cauterize it a second time on the same alumethen. Three lined scars appear. Therefore they will be more in the lower part of the back.
On the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When debility occurs in the bladder and softening from cold and humidities, until it does not retain weak urine, then cauterize it on the lower part of the sumen above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic area begin, and with a cauterizing iron to the right of the sumen, and another to the left of it: and let the length of this cauterization be according to the quantity of a knot of the thumb: and cauterize it with an inferior back cauterizing iron, or two cauterizing irons, if you need them: and let it be according to what preceded, the clavicular cauterizing iron.
On the method of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and humidities occur in the womb and it is prohibited from pregnancy because of that, and its menses are corrupted, and the provocation of them is delayed, and pain occurs to it at their arrival, then it is necessary to cauterize with three cauterizing irons around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and a cauterizing iron above the inferior back, or two cauterizing irons: and let the cauterizing iron be clavicular.
On the method of cauterizing an ankle in a state of dislocation.
When the mucous humidities are poured out at the ankle joint, and they become the cause of its exit from its place: and the sign of it is that one leg is prolonged over the other, when they are compared to each other: and the place of dislocation is found empty.
Therefore it is necessary that you cauterize the weak part over the ankle joint itself with a similar circular cauterization: after which you mark with a branding iron around the circumference of the joint, as it turns: and so that the joint falls in the middle of the circle.
If this cauterization is not present to you, then cauterize it with three cauterizations, with a large olive-shaped cauterization: and let the depth of the cauterization be according to the quantity of the thickness of the whole skin.
Then treat it, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for sciatica.
When pain occurs in the ankle joint, and its causes are cold and humidities: and it is treated with what we said in the division, and the treatment does not work, and it becomes chronic: then it is necessary that you loosen the weak part from gross humors with foul-smelling pills, or with artificial pills, and similar things. Then cauterize it.
And the method of cauterization for it is according to two methods: either cauterization with adhering medicines, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with fire is according to many methods.
Of which one is, that you cauterize over the ankle joint itself with three triangular cauterizations, according to this shape. And make for them a good depth, or a bad one. And let the space that is between all cautery be of the quantity of the thickness of a finger, and let the cautery be of olive.
Sometimes indeed the cauterization is made in the middle on the head of the same ankle. There are four cauteries.
And if you apply a cauterization with a circle, whose form has preceded in the cauterization of the dislocation of the ankle, one: so that the little circle contains the whole ankle.
And burn the thickness of the whole skin.
This is the method of cautery for sciatica, when the pain adheres to the ankle itself, and does not extend to the hip and thigh.
If it extends to the hip and thigh, then cauterize it with two cauteries above the hip, above the place to which that weakness points, in which is the pain, and your cauterization above the haunch four fingers towards the woody part for a little while: and let the cauterization be of a knife.
And let the depth of the cauterization be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
Which if the weakness indicates that the pain extends almost to the toes of the foot, then cauterize it there where it points with a cauterization of one point, or three, or four, or more, if it needs it.
And if it points to pain being under the knee towards the thigh, then cauterize it there with one knife-shaped cauterization.
And beware in every cauterization of yours, that you do not touch with the cauterization to the point that you burn a nerve, or a large artery, and drag through it above the weak nuisance evil, or contraction.
And I indeed have already seen one and another, of those who cauterized above the haunch, and finished in cauterization, and the thigh was inflamed, until a tumor followed to the foot, and the whole was perforated, and the whole foot was corrupted: then there occurred a loosening of the bowel, and death after that.
What if there is pain in two parts at the same time, cauterize both according to this method.
And certain wise men have said concerning the cauterization of the ankle, that the manner of this cauterization is thus. Make a drill similar to an iron one, whose diameter is half a palm, and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a date pit, or a little less: and inside that drill let there be a third drill.
And let the space that is between all the drills be by the quantity of a thumb knot: and let the drills be open on two sides: and let their height be as a knot, or two knots: and make for them a handle from iron decently fitted to the drills.
Then let it be ignited in fire, until it becomes red, and throws out sparks: then let it be placed upon the weak ankle, reclining on the healthy side. Cauterize it therefore with three round cauterizations in one place.
Then leave it for three days. Afterwards apply a plaster with butter: and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat it with ointment, until it is healed.
Albucasis says, we have used this type of cauterization little, on account of the terror of its appearance: and because we find few who dare to undertake it.
However, it is one of the good cauterizations for him who suffers it, and finds with it its place.
The cauterization with adhering medicines is, that you make two drills having a perforated armlet, into which descends a hinge of its door made from brass or iron, the length of a wall: of which in height there are two knots, or about that.
And let there be a space which is between the two quantities of the thickness of the finger, and let it be open below and above: and let that which they contain be next to one another, according to this form.
Then put it upon the axle of the instrument, while the weak part lies on the healthy side. And press your hand strongly upon the axle of the instrument. Then pour between the two circles from warm water, which has been heated with fire for a short time, and hold it for the quantity of an hour's time: and let the weak part tolerate its biting and burning, for it itself finds the biting as fire, until the biting subsides.
Then lift your hand with the instrument, and wipe away the warm water from the entire axle with sweet water: then leave it for three days.
And put upon it butter, until the blackness of the burn is removed: and leave it for some days, and pus will be cured from it. It is indeed the last in joining.
Then treat it with ointments, until it is healed.
What if the pain extends to the hip or the leg: make for it a plaster that contains water, according to what you did equally with the axle.
And this is the method of warm water: and I have already written it in the treatise on the correction of medicines. Take of alkaline substance and unslaked lime each one part: grind both, and put them in a new flask, whose lower part is perforated with one small hole, according to the quantity that the radius can enter: and put under the bottom of the flask another flask: and throw upon the alkaline substance and lime sweet water, which submerges both by a finger: after which you press it with your hand with good compression: and leave the flask until sharp water descends in the lower part of the flask.
Then gather all that water and pour it over another lime, and boil, until it is renewed.
For it will then be very strongly sharp, which is administered in many operations of medicine, and in the cauterization of the remaining members. Since it performs the operation of fire itself.
And there are medicines with which they cauterize, also such as tesie and mel of anacard, and lime with soap, so that both may be mixed together.
And Galen told of a certain man of the ancients, whose cure was such that it cured the pain of the hip and the vein of the thigh: and he declared its value to be great. And he said that it did not need another cure, and that he was healed by one means, until he told that he perhaps entered a warm bath, and came out of it already healthy.
And it is, that it be taken from the juice of the green, and if the green is not found, let the dry recent one be taken, and let much of it be rubbed with some fat, and put on the hip, where there is pain, or the leg, or in the hip, and let it be tied, and left for the quantity of three hours, or as long as he feels a weakening of the sensation of burning. Then put him into a bath.
When therefore his body becomes very sweaty, put him into the sun. For the pain returns, and is healed.
And know that it is not necessary to use a cauterization with these medicines, unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides said that the dung of capers, when with it the vein of the thigh is cauterized, is of service to it: and makes a cauterization in this manner. Let wool be taken and soaked in old oil, and put on the deep place, which is between the thumb of the foot, and the heel, and is closer to the heel.
Then take dry dung of a goat and set it on fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then put it on a cloth and leave it until it is extinguished. Then repeat it. Do not cease to do that until the sensation is felt up to the knee and the pain subsides.
And this method of cauterization is called the cauterization of the cow.
Of the cauterization of pain in the back.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back from many causes, either from a fall, or a blow, or excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and humid matter: and cauterization is not suitable, except in this single case, which occurs from the infusion of cold matter.
It is necessary therefore after the evacuation of the weak with fetid pills, and similar things, so that they are made on the back, where there is pain, three lines according to the width of the alum treatment itself, afterwards you mark with a cautery on each line five cauterizations, or more according to the quantity which comes from the tolerance of the weak by virtue of it: and let the cauterization be done with cauterized points.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauterizations, with a medial clavicular cautery, according to this method.
Of the method of cauterizing for the cure of gibbosity.
This disease often happens to small infants.
And the sign of this disease in children is: that it happens with a constriction in breathing at the time of elevation and movement: and you find on the last vertebra of the back and its knot, which has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When I raise that and make it a tool, then I cauterize it with a cauterizer which is a circle in this form.
And let the cauterization take hold equally over every part of the vertebrae: and if you cauterize around the vertebrae with a pointed cauterizer two or three lines: and let the points be close to one another.
Then treat the place until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware, lest you apply the cauterizer on the hump that forms during a spasm of the nerve.
On the method of cauterizing for gout and pains of the joints.
When the pains of the joints are from cold humidities that flow to whichever members of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is customary for physicians to call that specifically gout.
When therefore gout caused by cold is being treated with methods of treatment and the pains are not removed, then the cauterizer removes them.
And it is that you should cauterize him after evacuation around the joint of the foot with many cauterizers: and let the cauterizer be olive-shaped.
And if you indicate that there are points on the surface of the foot, then make with the cauterizer points. Which if the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, and it often happens, then cauterize it on every knee with three cauterizers or four on every side, with this same cauterizer for the hip.
If however many are needed for you by this cauterizer, then cauterize it. And do not insert your hand with the cauterizer, but rather to the thickness of the skin as much.
If however pains ascend to the knees and the back: then administer what we have said from cauterization in its chapter.
What if the pains are only in the hands, then punctures around the focuses, as two lines turn.
If however there remains from pain in the fingers, then puncture them, a puncture above every knot and above the palm of the hand.
If however pains ascend after days to the elbows or to the shoulders, then cauterize both from every part.
And do not evacuate the weak from a good regime, from the reception of medicines. For if a good regime is made, and the phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with the help of God together with this cauterization.
On the method of cauterizing for Hernias.
When a hernia occurs in the groin, and the intestine descends or the navel to the testicle, and it is that which begins nearby: then it is necessary to prescribe for the weak to omit eating on their day. And let them use lenients, so that feces may descend from their belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and prescribe to him, that he hold his breath, until it comes out, or the navel or intestine appears.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with a cauterizing iron under the hernia above the bone of the breast, with a mark whose extremities are similar to the middle of a circle at the top of the body.
Then ignite the cauterization iron, which is of this form, until it becomes white, and throws out sparks. Then reduce the intestine or navel to its concavity. Then let the servant put his hand over the place, so that the intestine does not come out: and you have now opened between the thighs of the weak, and placed under it a pillow, and one servant over his thighs, and another over his breast who holds the hands.
Then apply the cautery on that same sign, your hand with the cautery standing upright. And hold it, until you achieve the mouth with it: or turn it with it twice, if you have not achieved it at first even to the mouth.
And carefully observe from the exit of the intestine at the time of your cauterization, lest you burn it, and it comes out through that above into weakness or gangrene, or great evil.
And know that when you do not achieve the mouth with the cautery, your operation is of no use.
And it is fitting that the cautery for infants be subtle, according to their measure.
Then treat with the remaining ointment, until it is healed.
And let him be weak, lying on his back for forty days, until the wound is sewn.
And it is fitting that you put its nourishment for the length of time of its cure, which will soothe its stomach: so that the intestine does not come out at the anus and vomiting.
Then when he wants to get up after forty days, then administer a properly made bandage, and let him hold it for forty more days.
And he should be sparing of labor, and filling with food and drink, and violent voices.
For when he uses this regimen, thus will he be healed with a complete healing.
And I will speak of the cure for hernias with an incision in its own chapter.
When however hernias occur in the remaining belly, and are beginning, and it is seen that they do not increase, then cauterize the hernia with a round cautery according to its quantity: and let what is burned be one third of it. Then treat it, with that which we have said: and it will not increase.
And now some of the first ones have said: that a hernia should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it is marked with a cautery, and a line is applied along the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line is applied to the lower part. And put your hand in the middle with the cautery on the clavicle.
But the first cautery is easiest and best.
On the method of applying a cautery for pains caused by a fall or a blow.
Chapter 48.
When pain occurs in certain members from a fall or a blow, and the pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines is of no benefit, then it is necessary to apply a cautery with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery of each member be a second cautery according to its size, and its smallness, and its weakness, and its strength, and the location of the twisting and pain from it.
If therefore it is healed by the first cautery, it is good. If not: then repeat over the same place with a cautery.
For it is a custom of these pains that they change from one member to the one that is nearest to it. Wherefore it is necessary to follow them with a cautery until the weak part is healed.
On the method of applying a cautery for leprosy.
The leprous are sometimes helped by a very large cautery. And especially the type of leprosy that occurs due to the corruption of phlegm and melancholy: when therefore you use a cautery to treat it.
If therefore the leprosy is beginning, and you have treated it with what we said in the division, and it does not decrease, nor does it stop: and you apply on top of the weak part that comprehends the corruption over the entire complexion of it: then apply a cautery to him on the head with five cauteries: one on the middle knot of the head, and a second below that towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two above the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And finally put your hand with the cautery briefly, until it impresses a small impression on the mouth, and the cortices will be dislocated from it: so that the expiration of gross vapors is eased from it, and cauterize with the cautery also over the spleen itself, according to what has preceded.
But if the leprosy has already spread over the weak part, and appears manifestly: then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauterizations, which we mentioned in the head, and cauterize over the end of the nose, and with two cauterizations over the two jaws, and with two cauterizations over the vertebrae of the neck, and six over the vertebrae of the back, and one large one over the bone near the base of the tail and one over it, in the same almeidati: and two over the hips: namely one over each hip, and two over the knees: one over each knee, and two over the shoulders, and two over the elbows, and two over the tendernesses of his chest: and cauterize it over every joint, of the joints of the fingers of his hands and his feet: and cauterize over every heel of his feet, and the soles of his hands.
And beware of the nerves which are above the heel, that you do not burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a cautery over the bone of the chest, and another over the bone of the stomach, and another over the liver.
And know that the more you apply the cautery, the greater is the help, and the more beneficial it is.
And know that the weak person does not find pain in the cautery, as the healthy ones do: because his body is already numb.
And it is necessary that the cauterizations be of a size, and smallness according to the limbs and joints: according to what has preceded regarding the types of irons.
Then treat with a cauterization made from the powder of the herb with honey, and the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in a stupor.
When any member is in a stupor, and is treated with medicines, and oils, and plasters, and is not healed, then cauterize the stupified member with cauterizations, according to what the size of the member merits or its smallness.
And let your cauterization be shallow into the thickness of the skin for a little while. Then treat it with an ointment, until it is healed.
And when cauterization is applied for a stupor that occurs to the hand and foot, in the vertebrae of the back at the exit of the nerves which move that member: and the stupor is removed.
But truly let no one presume upon it, except he who is wise in the anatomy of the members and the exit of the nerves moving the body.
Chapter 51.
When Barbers becomes chronic and nothing helps it from the resources of medicine: then cauterize on it with a deep cauterization for a little while, according to the quantity of the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then treat it with the powder of the herb, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and pigeon's blood, and hyrundin's blood: let one part be of each: mix all these things, and apply them to a cloth, and stick to the place, until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for Cancer.
When Cancer is beginning and you want to restrain it: then cauterize it with a circular cauterization around its circumference, as it revolves.
Wise men have said that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
It does not seem to me, for I fear that it will become an ulcer, and I have already seen that happen many times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around it in a circle, as we have said, or with many cauteries.
On the method of cauterizing in those who are bald.
When someone has alopecia and it is slow to mature, either because of excessive flux causing it, or because of the weakness of old age, when he is decrepit and has little blood, or because of time and the need to hasten the maturation of alopecia, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries, puncturing many times. Then leave it alone. For it will hasten the maturation by itself.
If you want to make a perforation of it with a cautery, then ignite the cautery, which is of this form.
And place it in the middle of the alopecia, until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be from that which follows, weak, so that the flow of pus may be alleviated.
Then treat it until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing for a corrosive evil.
Chapter 54.
