And the generation of this watery collection, is from a weakness which happens to the testicles: for which reason this material flows forth to them. And sometimes it happens from a blow on the testicles.
And this humidity has many colors. For it is either of a yellowish color, or it is red with blood, or filthy, black, or it is watery white, and that is what is most.
And the signs by which it is known where the collection of water is, are these. For if it is in the white membrane which we have spoken of, then the tumor is round in length for a while as the figure of an egg: and the testicle does not appear, since the humidity contains it on all sides.
And if it is humidity in its own proper membrane, then the tumor is round with part of an egg, and on account of this a man thinks that it is another egg.
And if the humidity is between the skin of the testicles and the white membrane, then it falls under feeling.
When I apply my knowledge of the colour of humidity, then I examine the colour of humidity in an abscess with a square probe, whose shape precedes. Next to that which I observe as it exits the track of what has been inserted, I judge from that which is between itself.
When we proceed to a cure with iron, then it is necessary to prescribe to the weak, that they be bled if possible for them, and you see their body full.
Then he should be placed on his back on a high place slightly elevated, and many cloths should be put under him.
Then sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on his right side, who should extend his arm to one of the two sides of the skin of the testicles, and to the part of the navel.
Then take a broad spatula, and cut the skin of the testicles in the middle along the length, until almost to the pectine: and let the incision be according to the rectitude of the equidistant line which divides the skin of the testicles, until it reaches the white skin that surrounds: and clear away the same and observe, or beware lest you cut from this, as you cut the same: and your clearing should be where it is suspended with the egg more: and carefully examine with the clearing according to the quantity that is possible for you.
Then puncture the full skin with water with a wide puncture, and extract all the water.
Then separate between the two lips of the incision with forceps, and extend the skin to the top, and do not touch the skin that surrounds the testicles: and cut the skin as it is possible for you to cut it, either with its entirety or in a piece, especially the thin part. For if you do not carefully examine, in the incision of it there is no security, lest water return.
If however the egg emerges outward from its skin during the time of your operation: then when you complete the incision of the womb, reduce it. Then bring together the two lips of the skin of the testicles with a suture.
Then cure it as the remaining wounds, until it is healed.
What if you find the egg corrupted from blackness of another, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels, which are the suspensors, fearing a flow of blood.
Then cut off the testicle with its suspensor, and extract the egg: afterwards cure it with what we have said.
If indeed water is collected in the two parts, then know that there are two branches: cut therefore one part equally as you did in the other.
And if it is equal to you, so that it is one operation, then do it: afterwards wipe away the blood. And insert into the incisions a thread steeped in oil, or in rose oil: and put on top of it another thread which you have steeped in wine and oil, and spread it over the two testicles, and the navel: and put above double cloths, and they are poultices: and tie them above with a bandage, which is having six according to this form.
Then let two cloths be taken, and they should suck, and the threads which have been steeped should fill them, according to this likeness: and let extremities be made which are pressed from a cot, or a wet thread: and let them be bound with a bandage on the loins of the arms: and one extremity should reach to the thigh up to the back, and the second should reach to the part of the chest: and two extremities over the two hips below, and two other extremities over the two groins, and all the bandage should be bound in the loins of the arms.
And when this hernia is artificially treated with a cautery at the place of the incision with iron: and it is, that you take a sharp knife-cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles: and it is ignited, according to what we have described: until when it is detected, a white tissue containing water: then take the cautery, according to this method.
The Greek letters are assimilated.
Then perforate with it that tissue, and it is ignited, until all the moisture goes out.
Then extend the tissue with forceps, and scratch with a sharp ignited cautery, and cut it according to what is possible for you, until you eradicate the whole of it.
And beware lest the fire touch it.
And know that this operation is safer, and less prone to a flow of blood, and better than the operation with incision.
If however it shows opposition to you at the time of incision, or at the time of cautery, a hot aposteme, or a flow of blood, or something else: then it is necessary that you cure what shows opposition to you from that with a cure which is suitable for it, according to what has been said before.
But if he is weak and fearful, and does not expect more than this operation, on account of his horror: then administer the perforation according to what I describe it: and it is.
When it is confirmed to you by what we have said concerning the signs, that the hernia is watery: then it is necessary that you make the weak person sit on an elevated seat.
Then puncture the aposteme in its lower part with a broad spatula: and make the puncture according to the length of the body, and let it be open wide, until all the water runs out.
Then put on the place a dressing, and bind it, and let it be so that the remainder of the water runs out: then treat it, until the wound is healed.
If however there is a contrariety to the egress of water at the time when you perforate it: and it is not except on account of this, because the white pad makes a contrariety in the orifice of the wound, and prohibits the exit of the water: then it is necessary that you insert a feather into the wound, or an instrument with which water of dropsy is extracted, whose form has preceded: or add for a short while in the operation of the wound.
And you should know that the water returns and accumulates after six months, or around that time. When therefore it accumulates, then it will perforate according to the same method, and the weak days will pass.
Chapter 63.
On the treatment of a fleshy tumor.
Know that in the incision above this tumor, there is a fear of inducing a deadly peril in many dispositions. Wherefore it seems to me that its abandonment is more beneficial for the health from it.
And I recall an operation on it, and the appearance of a postulate.
I say therefore, that many gatherings occur in the bodies, from which the testicles are composed: and this is caused by many reasons, namely.
Or from an excess of sharp or sour humors, which flows to the testicles. Or from a blow.
And the color of the gathering is according to the color of the body, and no pain is found in it: and it is a serious gathering.
And perhaps it is a stone-like gathering, whose color is dark, and there is no sensation in it.
And sometimes it happens from a knotting of the arteries, and their inflation: as has already been mentioned earlier: or from an inflammation of the veins.
That which therefore is from them by an inflation of the arteries, is recognized by the condition of the gathering, when you press on it with your fingers. And it is not suitable that you touch it directly.
That which is made from the inflammation of veins, does not disappear because of compression with the fingers.
And now it is possible that a section is made on this species, and on the remaining flesh: and it is, as one cuts the skin of the testicles. Then extend the eyelid upwards, and extract it with a white sifauch: and free the suspensory membrane from the vessel, and tie the vessels: and cut the suspensory membrane after you have freed it from every part of the eyelid.
If then the eyelid is consolidated with those born flesh, then it is necessary that you attract the eyelid, and cut it.
And if there is an adherence of something from the siphac, or in that which is between the vessels: then it is necessary that you free the entire adherence, and cut it with a round incision.
If however there is a nativity of flesh in the place of adherence which is behind: then it is necessary that you cut all of it, and extract the eyelid, as we have said.
When therefore your operation is complete, then fill the wound with wool steeped in rose oil and wine: afterwards treat it with the remaining treatment, until it heals.
Chapter 64.
On the treatment of Rams, which is with Vites.
Uitis is an unturned aposteme, a certain unturning similar to a bunch, with softening of the testicles: and it makes movement and exercise difficult on the weakened area, and walking.
And in the cure of this sickness is fear, because of the memory of that which has come before.
It is truly necessary that we speak of the operation according to what the first ones did.
I say therefore, that it is necessary for the weak one to sit on a raised seat. Then strike the suspension of the testicles to the lower parts. Then hold the skin of the testicles with your fingers, with the instruments that are closest to the rod: and let another servant hold it, and stretch it with a vehement stretching.
Then cut with a broad sharp spatula a cross-section directly through the vessels, until they are laid bare.
Then scratch from every part, as we have told you in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples.
Afterwards fix in them a needle in which is double thread, and tie it in the first of the places to which the vessels are attached: and tie it again at the last of them. Then cut it in a straight middle section according to the length of the body, and extract what is gathered from foul corrupt humors.
Then treat the wound with the treatment of other wounds, in which you wish to generate a sanative, so that the vessels which nourish one of the testicles fall away. For it is not an evil through that.
If however the vessel happens to all the vessels, then it is necessary that the testicles with the vessels be extracted for this: so that the egg is not deprived of nourishment, on account of the incision, and wither, or dry up, and is not a help with them.
Chapter 65.
Of the treatment of Intestinal wounds.
The outcome of this wound is from a section, which happens in the sifac expanded over the belly in the groin area from the navel of the belly.
Because the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles. And this rupture is either from the sifac or from its extension.
And these two types occur from many causes: either from a blow, or a jump, or a shout, or the lifting of a heavy thing, and similar things.
And the sign is when it is from the extension of the ankle. It is what happens gradually over a long period of time, and does not happen suddenly: and it is an equal aposteme towards the deep, therefore because the ankle compresses the intestine.
And its sign is when it is from a section of the ankle, because it makes happen from the beginning a vehement pain suddenly: and it is a diverse aposteme, appearing under the skin nearby: and that is because of the exit of the intestine, and its course to the exterior of the ankle.
And sometimes it goes out with the intestine a knob: and this is called Ramex intestinalis, and zirbia: and sometimes it happens with bloating.
And sometimes dung runs into the intestine, and is retained there: and it is with that a weakness of the flanks: for it makes happen a bad pain, and especially when it is pressed.
And in the cure of the species of this disease with iron there is fear: wherefore it is necessary that the case be cautioned in it.
And the method of operation is, that you instruct the weak person, to reduce the intestine with his hand to the interior of its own concavity, if it has fallen back. Then he should be lifted up over his neck between your hands: and his legs should be elevated.
Then extend the skin that follows the skin to the upper parts, and cut the skin of the testicles along its entire length. Then fix on both lips of the incision hooks, according to which you indicate to open the incision with them: and let the incision be according to the quantity that is possible, so that the egg can come out from it.
Then scratch the ankle and what is under the skin of the testicles, until when the white ankle is uncovered, hard on every side: then insert your index finger in what follows the testicle, in what is between the ankle and the white, which is under the skin of the egg, and between the ankle and the second, and release with it the adhesion that is in the posterior part of the egg.
Then move with your right hand to the inner skin of the testicles: and with this extend the white membrane upwards, with your left hand: and lift the vein with the membrane to the part of the incision: and instruct the assistant, to extend the vein upwards: and you loosen the adhesion, which is behind the completed solution.
And search with your fingers, that there is not something from the intestine involved in the white hard membrane of the spleen. If however you find something of it: then push it to the lower abdomen.
Then take a needle, in which is a thick thread, made a ligature from ten threads: and introduce it at the back of the last membrane, that is, of the tunic, which is under the skin of the testicles which follows the incision: then cut the ends which project from the thread, until there are four threads. Then arrange some of them over others with a figure that is in the shape of a cross: and tie with them the membrane, of which we spoke, which is under the skin of the testicles with a vehement ligature, until none of the vessels, which nourish them can send to them anything: so that there does not happen from it a hot apostema. And put again a second ligature outside the first ligature, being less than two fingers in length from it. And after these two ligatures release from the membrane, which is under the skin of the testicles, a quantity the size of a finger: and cut the rest entirely around, and take away the vein.
Then sew in the lower part of the skin of the testicles at the incision, from which runs blood and serum: as we have described in what was previously said.
Then administer a wool submerged in oil, and put it on the wound: and administer the ligature that we described. And when the white tonsil is cauterized, which we have mentioned, after its incision, fearing a flow of blood. For this often happens. And release the ligament, until it falls by itself.
If however its fall is delayed, then let it be soaked with warm water: and put on it what we have said, until it falls.
Then treat the wound with the remainder of the treatment of wounds, until it is cured.
Chapter sixty-six.
On the Lance-shaped Instrument.
In this lance I have not seen anyone who has dared to undertake its treatment with iron.
And the first ones said, that it is done as we have described in the lance which is with a vine. Which is to bind the vessels after the incision over them with ease below: then cut in the middle, and treat afterwards with that which opens it, until the vessels fall: and treat the wound, according to what we have said, until it is healed.
Chapter sixty-seven.
On the rupture that occurs in the groins.
When a rupture occurs in the groins, as we have said, and the place protrudes, and nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles: and if it does descend, it is very little, and returns every hour: but if the time with this condition is prolonged, a fissure is added in the sifach, until the intestines descend into the sifach.
And it happens due to the extension of the sifach, which is in the groins, as we have said. Which is because the sifach extends: then it becomes soft, and the place becomes inflamed, and protrudes.
And its treatment is with a cautery, as the description of it has preceded.
And sometimes it is treated with iron, in this manner: and it is done so that the weak person lies on his back between your hands. Then cut the place of the rupture and the prominent part, a cross-section in width, according to the quantity of three fingers.
Then pull the Alsifak and those that are under the skin, until when it is stretched the white Sifach, which is under the skin that follows it.
Then take the rasp, and put it on the prominent place of the Sifach, and press it to the depth of the wound.
Then sew two prominent places on the extremity of the rasp from the Sifach, and join one of them with the other with a suture: then extract the extremity of the rasp.
And do not cut the Alsifak at all, nor stretch the groin, nor anything else, as I have made you know in the treatment of intestinal rupture.
Then treat it with the treatment of wounds. When you cut the threads, clean it, and restore the wound, until it becomes consolidated.
For the Sifach is contracted, and the prominence of the Rupture is not increased.
And cauterization is better in this place: because it is closer to health.
Chapter 68.
On the softening of the skin of the testicles.
The skin of the testicles often becomes softened in some men, because of which the flesh that is between them becomes softened, and their appearance becomes foul.
Therefore it is necessary for him who is asked to cure it, to make the weak one lie on his back, and to cut all the skin that has been softened above the natural skin.
Then bring together the two lips with a suture: and if necessary, first close the excess of softened skin with three or four sutures, and tighten the suture.
Then cut between the sutures.
Then treat it with the treatment of other wounds, until it is healed, and the threads fall out.
Chapter 69.
On Castration.
Know that castration is forbidden by our law, and because of it I would be allowed not to mention it in my book, and its mention would not be necessary except for two reasons.
One of which is that it is a thing in the science of medicine when one is questioned about it, and so that he may know the cure for one to whom it happens.
And the second reason is that we often need to castrate certain animals for our use by it, such as donkeys, goats, and cats, and similar animals.
I say therefore, that castration is performed in two ways. Or by extraction. Or by incision and cutting.
In that which is done by extraction, the method of operation is: that we make the animal sit in hot water until its testicles soften and relax and hang, then we extract them with our hand until they dissolve and do not appear to the touch.
In castration by incision and cutting, it is necessary that you hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the suspensor, and cut above all one ovary with a single cut, until when two ovaries proceed: then incise those after you have excavated both, and do not leave on them anything from silk except subtle silk, which is above the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than that which is done by extraction: because extraction perhaps leaves something of the testicles, for which reason the animal desires intercourse.
Then treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter 70.
On the treatment of the Hermaphrodite of two kinds.
Hermaphrodite from urine is second in two modes. The defect of theirs is that which appears in the space that follows, or on the skin of the testicles, between the two testicles, a figure similar to a woman's vulva, in which there are hairs: and sometimes urine runs out from that which is on the skin of the testicles.
In women however there is one species, and it is a woman's vulva above the pubic area just like the testicles of a small man entirely, standing out to the exterior: of which one is like the penis of a man, and two like two testicles.
And the treatment of the three species, two from men and one species from women, is: that it is necessary to cut away the excess flesh, until the impression of them disappears. Then treat them with the cure of remaining wounds.
In the second species of men, from which urine exits, which is on the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any treatment at all.
Chapter 71.
Concerning the cutting of the Tentiginis, and the prominent flesh in the vulvas of women.
The prepuce perhaps is added over the natural part, until it becomes deformed and its appearance is foul: and sometimes it is magnified in certain women to such a degree, that it expands like in men, and reaches to the coitus.
It is necessary therefore to hold the excess of the prepuce with the hand, or with a hook, and cut: and do not cease in the cutting, especially in the depth of the root: so that there does not occur a flow of blood.
Then treat it with the treatment of wounds, until it heals.
The flesh that is born, is a flesh that grows in the opening of the womb, until it fills it: and perhaps it comes out to the exterior similar to a tail: and because of this some of the first call it a caudal affliction. It is necessary therefore that we incise it as we incise the tenthigin, and we should treat it until it is healed.
On the treatment of Alratica, which is a woman's ulcer that is not perforated.
Chapter 72.
Alratica is, that it is a woman's ulcer not perforated, or it is a small opening. And it is either natural or accidental.
Accidental is from the sickness that precedes it: and this indeed occurs either from flesh born added, or from sifach subtle, or from spissus: and it happens either in the depth of the matrix, or in its sides, or in the upper part of it, or in the lower part of it: and prohibits coitus and impregnation, and childbirth, and perhaps prohibits menstruation.
And its recognition is made by the appearance of the obstetrician, if the obstruction is apparent nearby.
If it is not apparent, then examine it with your fingers, or with a rod.
If the obstruction is from subtle sifach and it is near the two lips: then touch and disrupt it.
And it is, that you place a poultice on the two lips.
Then put your indexes of both hands together, and let the woman be on her back with her thighs spread apart. Then stretch the two lips with force, until the subtle sifach is disrupted and the obstruction is opened.
Then take a wool, and soak it in oil, and put it on the place: and let the woman apply it every day, so that the place is not consolidated with vice.
If the sifach is thick and spissus, then it is necessary to cut it with a spatula like a myrtle leaf.
If the obstruction is from flesh born, then suspend it with hooks, and incise it: and let there be with you medicines which calm the flux of blood without biting, such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and thus mixed with the whites of eggs.
Then administer a cannula made of lead, so that the wound does not heal quickly, it will hold for some days; and administer a bandage made from dry linen, then the rest will be cured by treatment, until it is healed.
And when there is a growth in the matrix of native flesh of other things, it is necessary therefore that they be cut according to this method: since there is not an apostema which is cancerous for an apostema is indeed cancerous which is in the matrix, let there not be done with iron altogether.
Chapter 73.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, Athehel, and Bothor of rubies in the wounds of women.
Hemorrhoids are indeed openings of the veins, until a lot of blood flows out from them continually.
When therefore hemorrhoids become chronic, they become hard: and I have already spoken of the division of their types, and their signs: and I will say here which of them receive treatment, and which do not.
I say therefore, that hemorrhoids which are in the opening of the matrix and do not appear to the sense, then there is no treatment for them with iron.
But those of them which are in the opening of the matrix, upon which the sense falls, are those which can be treated.
It is necessary therefore that the woman be put into a cold house. Then extend the hemorrhoids with the fingers, or with coarse cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Then sprinkle over them at the flow of blood from one powder of incisions without sharpness: such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and incense, and similar to these.
Then press her feet against the wall for one hour. Afterwards put her into cold water.
If the flow of blood persists: then make her sit in a decoction of sumach, and a broth of pomegranates, and gall, and similar things.
Then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it over its back.
If therefore blood is drawn with it, it is good: and if not, make the ventoses and the breasts adhere to the back without scarification.
Then take wool and soak it in the juice of tarathit, or the juice of arnoglossa, or the juice of the branches of alaulat, that is, aglanter, Pontic wine, and make it adhere to the place.
When therefore the apostema rests, then treat the place with ointments, until it is healed.
The Albarth verily is a red color like the heads of alhassa, and is of rough appearance.
It is necessary therefore that you cut what appears from it, according to what I said equally in the case: and treat it, until it is healed.
Chapter 23.
Of the perforation of the uterus which occurs in the matrix.
There occur in the matrix many kinds of apostemas, such as cancer, and apostema of stone, and ulcers, and adubelati, and alekilati, that is, herpes, aestiomemus, and fistulas, and hemorrhoids, and ragadiae, and thelil, and hot apostema.
And I have already spoken of all these diseases and their kinds, and the signs of them, and their cures in division: it is necessary that I speak in this treatise of hot apostema which occurs in the matrix, when it is one of the apostemas which collect blood, and you should know how its opening is done with iron.
It is necessary therefore that you consider. Then if the pain of the apostema at its beginning is acute with its percussion, and inflammation, and fever: and you see it being red: if the sensation falls upon it, then do not hasten with its perforation: and treat it with that which helps against maturation, until when the acuteness of the accidents subsides.
Then it is suitable to make the woman sit on a seat which has two seats, and she should lean back or lie on her back, and bring her feet to the lower part of the abdomen: and her hips should be expanded, and she should put her arms under her thighs, and tie them with a convenient ligature to that.
Then the midwife should sit at the right side, and administer the instrument by which the orifice of the matrix is opened.
And it is suitable when you are about to administer this instrument, that you fix with the radius the depth of the woman's matrix: so that what enters from the instrument is not more than the depth of the matrix, and harms the weak.
If the instrument is more than the depth, then it is suitable that you put pads on the surface of the depth of the matrix: so that the entrance of the whole instrument into the depth of the matrix is prohibited: and it is suitable that a loop which runs on the instrument be placed from the upper side: and that it hold the instrument, and that the operator turn the loop, until the depth of the matrix is opened.
When therefore the exit appears and is touched by the hand, and it is gentle and soft: then it is suitable that you cut it at its head with a broad spatula.
When therefore the sanies is evacuated, then it is suitable that you put on the wound a plaster submerged in rose oil: or green oil, in which there is some astringency: and put the plaster, and extract the section from the depth of the matrix.
And put outside on the matrix, and on the pubes a clean wool submerged in water, in which mallows have been boiled.
Then it should be treated after two days with an ointment that is suitable for it, until it is healed.
And when the matrix and wound are washed, then a clyster is applied with water and honey; afterwards with water in which the root of lily or long aristolochia has been boiled; afterwards it returns to an ointment.
What if the wound has been hidden within the matrix, then it is necessary that you forbid the cure of it with iron, but rather cure it with what we have said in the division.
Chapter 70.
The doctrine of obstetrics, how they medicate living embryos, according to a figure not natural, having come out.
It is necessary for the obstetrician to know first the figure of a naturally born child.
From the signs of it are, that when you see a woman pressed at the lower parts, and she desires to smell the air, and is relieved by what is above her from the birth, and the exit of the embryo is hastened: then know that this birth is according to the natural figure, and its exit is over its head, and the afterbirth with it: or hanging, or suspended from the navel.
When you see these signs, then it is necessary that her womb be pressed, so that the embryo may come down quickly.
For when it comes down over its head, the afterbirth comes down with it, and is cleansed from those superfluities of a good cleansing.
But that which is besides this birth, is unnatural, not to be praised.
For when the fetus comes out over its feet, and its body comes out before its head, and its feet, and one of its hands, or one of its feet: or its head and its hands come out: or its belly comes out: and perhaps it turns back over its neck, and similar things from unnatural figures.
It is necessary therefore for the obstetrician to be prudent, subtle in all these things, and to beware of error and deception: and I am showing the whole figure of them, and how the device is in it, and it is signified by that, and stands upon it.
When the fetus moves up above its head with its natural movement, and presses upon the woman, and parturition becomes difficult for her, and you see her strength is already weakened: then make her sit on a seat, or let women hold her: and fumigate her vulva with decocted fenugreek, and with humid oils.
Then the midwife should insert her fingers into the little spatule, and find the secundina with it, and cut it with her nail, until what is in it runs out from the humidity: and press the belly of the woman, until the fetus comes down.
And if it does not come down, then it is necessary that the woman be given a clyster of fenugreek mucilage, with sesame oil.
Then order her after the clyster, that she be compressed: and make her sneeze with conditis, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour. For the fetus will come out immediately.
What if the two hands of the fetus come out first, then it is necessary that you reduce them with ease little by little. And if it does not pass into the birth passage, then put the woman on a seat, and lift her feet up: then strike the seat against the ground: and let the woman be held, so that she does not fall with the striking.
If therefore the hands do not come out, and the fetus dies: then cut them off, and extract the rest of the fetus: and tie its hand with a cloth, and pull it out gently: for it will come out.
The fetus coming out over its own feet. When the fetus comes out over its own feet, then it is necessary that you push them upwards: then turn the fetus little by little: afterwards pull it evenly.
Then take one of its feet and stretch it out little by little.
When they go out as far as the hips, then order him to compress it, and make him sneeze with the condiment: for it will come out, if God wills.
And if it does not come out with what we have described, then reduce the fomentation little by little, until you put it in its natural shape. For it will then come out with an easy exit.
What if it is prohibited with all that we have described: then take from the mucus of the altea, and the oil of sisamine, and dissolved gum: and pound all in a mortar with a good pounding: then smear the vulva of the woman, and her lower belly. Then make her sit in warm water, until she obtains an enema.
When you see that her lower parts are already warmed, then make for her a suppository of myrrh: and apply it. When she has held the suppository for one hour, then make her sit on a seat. Then make her sneeze: and pinch its mouth and nose: and press the lower part of the belly with an easy compression. For the feces will come out immediately.
The fetus comes out over the knees and hands. When it comes out according to this shape, then she will insert her hands gradually while introducing them. Then the woman will be lifted up over her neck, and her feet will hang down to the lower parts: and she herself will lie on a bed, and clasp her hands. Then press above her belly little by little. Then extract what is under her feet from the dusty things, until it is prepared in the lower part. What if the fetus does not come out, then take her feet, and move them with a vehement movement. Then press what is above the pubic area gradually, until the fetus ascends to the upper parts. Then he should insert his hands and gradually straighten the fetus, and command the woman to compress, until the fetus comes out.
The fetus exits hanging crosswise from the hands. It is placed in the reduction of his hand. If however he cannot reduce it, then let him lift the woman, and have her walk.
If indeed she is not able to walk, then let him make her lie on a bed, and shake her thighs with violent shaking.
Then administer the ointment that you have prepared from mucilages.
Which if it receives the birth, then make her sit on a seat. Then attend to the reduction with the hands, and straighten the fetus according to its natural shape: and make the woman sneeze, and command her to compress herself, until it comes out.
The fetus exits with its neck stretched out, hands extended, and its face towards the mother's back. It is necessary that the midwife hold the fetus's hand, then slowly turn it around, and straighten it with ease.
When it is straightened, then put on its neck what we have mentioned, made from oil and mucilages.
Then command her to move gradually. When you have done that, then make her sit on a seat, and command her to lean to the right side. Then command her to compress herself: and make her sneeze with effort.
The prepared fetus exits on the side. When it descends to the opening of the womb in this manner with the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth with your nail, until it comes out from the moisture.
If I suspend it over the face of the fetus, and its neck, then cut it from the navel: so that it is not retained, and dies.
Then push the fetus to the inside, until you place it according to what is fitting: and instruct the woman to press herself several times: for it will come out by itself with a light exit.
The exit of twins, or of many fetuses. Know that twins are born many times: and when three, and four are born. But truly that is extraordinary, and rarely happens.
Five is a thing beyond nature, and they do not live thoroughly: and the afterbirth contains them, however many they are multiplied, one secundine: and they are separated by the navel, distinguishing between them the ligature at the navel of each of them.
And sometimes they come out just as one fetus comes out by the natural and easy way: and they come out with an unnatural exit, as we have described.
What if some of them are difficult at birth, and they reach that which we have spoken of from unnatural figures, then treat them as we have described: and let there be a subtle and skilled midwife, and she will do what she does with ease and slowness, and will guide according to every figure with what is prepared for her from guiding ingenuity for health.
The memory of that which is formed in the womb from embryos, and are aborted.
Sometimes one is formed in the womb, and two, and three, and four, and five, and six, and seven, and more than ten: and it has been verified by me, that a woman aborting has expelled seven, and another fifteen, all formed.
Which was done by the measurement of the glorious wise one.

Chapter 76, Head or Chapter Seventy-six, Head
On the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you treat a dead fetus with what I have said in the division on medication, and it does not come out, and you are compelled to use an operation with the hand, then it is necessary that you consider.
If the woman is of sound strength and is not with any of the accidents on account of which loss is feared for her: then it is necessary that the woman breathe again on a bed, on her back, and her head be inclined downward, and her thighs be elevated: and an assistant hold her from two sides, or she be tied to the bed, so that her body not be extruded during the extraction of the fetus.
Then the mouth of the matrix should be moistened with humid oils, with mucus of altea, and fenugreek, and seed of flax.
Then the midwife should anoint her hand with these oils and mucus: then she should introduce it into the matrix with ease. Then she should search with it for the place where she will fix the hooks of the fetus, and the places convenient to that.
Consider then, if the fetus is prepared to descend on its head: then fix the hooks in its eyes, or in its neck, or in its mouth, or in its palate, or under its beard, or in its throat, or in places near the ribs, and under the false ribs.
If however it has descended on its feet, then in its chest, and its middle ribs.
And it is necessary that she hold the hook with her right hand: and place its curvature in that which is between the fingers of the left hand: and introduce with the hand with ease, and fix the hook in any of those places which we have said, until it reaches the empty space.
Then he should put another hook in opposition to it, or a third, if necessary, so that the contraction is equal and does not incline to one side.
Then it should be extended with an equal extension, and the extension is not just according to straightness, but rather it moves to every part, so that its exit is alleviated, as happens with a tooth during its extraction.
And it is necessary in what is between them, that the extension is softened. What if a part of it is retained, then it is necessary that the midwife anoints some fingers with oil and inserts them from the side, so that she turns it out with them, what was retained.
If therefore a part of the fetus comes out, then the hooks are changed to another place which is higher: do this until the whole fetus comes out.
If therefore a hand comes out before the other, and it is not possible to reduce it, because of its constriction: then it is necessary that a cloth is wrapped around it. Then pull it out until when the whole thing comes out, cut it at the joint of the foot, or at the elbow: and thus it is necessary that you do the same with the other hand, and with the two feet.
If the head of the fetus is large, or it meets with constriction at the exit, or there is water accumulated in its head: then it is necessary that a sharp Spatumile is inserted between the fingers, and searches with it the head, and extracts the water: or it breaks it with an instrument which is called Almisdac, whose form comes with the forms of other instruments in the chapter that follows.
Similarly, do it if the fetus is of a large-headed nature, then it is necessary that you cut the shoulder blade: or extract it with a misdach, as we have said. Then you pull the bones with forceps.
What if the head comes out and it is narrowed at the armpit then it will be found until the moisture that is in the chest is poured out.
If however it does not become compact and nor obstructs the exit: then cut the head bit by bit, according to that which is possible for you.
What if the lower part of the belly is an apostema, or there is dropsy in it: then it is necessary that you perforate it, until moisture runs out from it.
If indeed the fetus is above its feet, then its extraction is easy, and its direction to the mouth of the matrix is light.
If however it is narrowed at the belly or chest: then it is necessary that you extract it with a cloth which you have wrapped over your hand: and find the belly or chest, until what is in them runs out.
If however the rest of the limbs are removed and the head returns: then the Midwife should insert her left hand. If therefore the mouth of the matrix is open, then she should insert her hand into the depth of the matrix, and seek with it the head, and draw it out with her fingers to the mouth of the matrix: then she should insert in it one hook, or two hooks, and draw it out with them.
What if the mouth of the matrix is narrowed, on account of the hot apostema that has happened to it: then it is not necessary that she should labor over it, but rather it is necessary then to administer an effusion of humid things, of ointments: and administer plasters: and sit in waters which soften and moisten.
What if the fetus is on its side, then it is possible that it can be straightened: then administer what we have said regarding a living fetus.
What if it is not possible, then cut it bit by bit, and extract it.
And it is suitable that you should not leave anything from the second intestine inside at all.
When you have completed your operation, then administer what we have said regarding the hot apostemes that occur in the matrices.
What if a flow of blood occurs, then let it be stopped with astringent waters, and administer the remainder of the cure.
And I have indeed already seen a woman, in whose womb a dead fetus was, then she became pregnant on top of it with another, afterwards another fetus also died. Therefore, a postulate occurred to her after a long time on her navel, and it became inflated, until it was opened: and it began to emit pus.
I was called therefore to her cure, and I treated her for a long time: and the wound was not consolidated.
I placed therefore on it some strong attractive plasters: and the bone went out from its place. Then several days passed for her, and another bone came out. I was amazed therefore by this, since there is no bone in the womb.
I thought therefore that they were from the bones of a dead fetus.
I probed the wound, and I extracted many bones, with the woman being in a better state of health: and she lived for a long time afterwards, and a little pus was discharged from the place.
And I have not confirmed this strange thing, except that there is science and assistance in it, for what the medical artisan administers with his hand from the cure.
Chapter 78.
Of the forms of necessary instruments for the extraction of a fetus.
The shape of the Vertigo by which the matrix is opened.
This figure below is the form of a stretcher, to which are equal two books, on which there are two equal joints at the ends of two wooden pieces. The treatment for this Vertigo requires that it should be finer than a strictorium: and that it is made either from ebony or from boxwood.
And the width of all the wood is about two fingers, and the thickness of each of them is about one finger, and the length of each of them is a palm and a half: and in the middle of the two pieces of wood there are two additions made from the same type of wood, which have already been fixed to both, whose length is half a palm and a little more: and the width of each is about two fingers or a little more.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the matricis, so that it opens with them when you turn the two Vertigines.
Another form similar to that, finer and lighter.
Let it be made from ebony wood or boxwood, according to the likeness of the forceps. However, on the extremity of it there are two additions, as you see here above: and the length of each addition is about a palm: and the width of each is two fingers.
When you use it to open the matrix, then make the woman sit on a bed, with her feet hanging, and what is between her thighs open. Then insert these two connected additions into the matrix: and you hold the extremity of the instrument below between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with forceps, equally according to the quantity that you need from the opening of the mouth of the matrix, until the midwife does what she wants.
The shape of another Vertigo which the ancients called the Shape of the Impeller by which the fetus is expelled.
The shape of the Almisdac, with which the large head is pressed: and it is similar to forceps, which have teeth on the extremity, as you see.
And whenever a dressing is applied, such as forceps according to this shape, as you see, which has teeth like the teeth of a saw, with which it is cut and crushed.
The form of a staple having one spike.
The form of a staple having two spikes.
The form of a spatula having two extremities for cutting off the head.
The form of two broad spatulas.
All these instruments are exercised, and the more their kinds are multiplied, and the more they are prepared by the artisan, the swifter he is to his operation, and the higher he is among men, on account of their quantity.
Do not therefore despise any of these instruments, so that it may be prepared with you. Their necessity is indeed inescusable.
Chapter 78.
On the extraction of the placenta.
When the placenta is retained with the afterbirth, then it is necessary to advise the weak, so that it retains its own breathing. Then make it sneeze with condiments: and press your hand over its mouth, and nostrils. If therefore it comes out through this, it is good.
If not: then take a pot, and perforate in its cover a hole: and put in it heating herbs of the matrix, such as calamint, rue, and dill, and chamomile, and sesam, and lignea cassia, and centaury: take all these herbs, or some of them, and submerge them with water, and put them over fire.
Then put a bulb of reeds over the hole of the pot's cover, and another extremity into the mouth of the matrix: and hold it until the vapor penetrates to the concoction of the matrix.
Then make it sneeze, as we have said. For the second one will go out with ease.
If however it remains after this treatment, and does not come out: then instruct the Midwife to immerse her hand in oil of sesame, or mallow. Then let her insert it into the vulva, and seek with it the Second one. When therefore she has found it, then let her take it, and pull it out little by little.
If however it is attached in the depth of the womb, then let her insert her hand, according as we have described, until when she finds the Second one, and pulls it out little by little according to what is right, so that the womb does not fall with violent pulling: indeed it is necessary, that it be turned with ease to the right and left sides: then let there be added to the quantity of the pulling. For it will detach itself then, and be freed, and come away from the adherence.
Which if the mouth of the womb is constricted, as we have already described: treat it with sneezing, and from a medication of oil with herbs.
If however it does not come out with all that we have described, then beware lest you fatigue yourself over it in the repetition of the extraction.
It is necessary indeed, that what comes out from it to the mouth of the womb, you tie to the thigh of the woman. Then anoint her with the ointment Tetrapharmakon. For it will putrefy it after some days, and dissolve it, and bring it out.
Truly when it has putrefied, a bad smell rises from it to the stomach and head, and harms that weak woman. It is necessary therefore that fumigations suitable for it be administered.
Certain of the ancients have already experienced the fumigation of nasturtium and fig and sycamore.
The shape of an instrument with which a woman is fumigated for retention of the secundina and menses.
Let it be made from a bowl similar to an alcama or from clay: and let the broad extremity be placed over the fire: and let the fumigation be put on the coals: let her hold it, until that fumigation is consumed: and let another be repeated.
Chapter 79.
Of the cure of an anus not perforated.
Many boys are born, and their anus is not perforated, whom the subtle sifac has already closed. It is necessary therefore, that the midwife should perforate that sifac with her finger: and if not, she should perforate it with a sharp spatulum: and let her beware of the arm, lest it touch.
Then put on it a wool cloth soaked in wine and oil. Then treat it with ointments, until it is healed.
If however you fear that it will close, then put in the hole a small tube of lead for many days, and let it be removed when the boy wants to evacuate.
And now closure of the anus also occurs from consolidation of a wound, or an abscess. It is necessary therefore that the consolidation be cut, then treated with what we said regarding the cure and lead.
Chapter 80.
Of the cure of fistulas which occur in the lower part.
The fistulas that occur in the lower parts are a knotting and a thickening which occur near the anus or in the space of one of the parts: and it is one fistula or several.
When therefore that knotting becomes old, it opens, and a watery white humidity or subtle pus runs out from it.
And when there are some of these fistulas that penetrate. Therefore penetrating fistulas are recognized by that which exits from the evacuation and flatulence, when the weak one uses the evacuation, and perhaps exits from the worms.
And there are of them fistulas when they penetrate in space up to the bladder and up to the passage of the rod. And there are of them penetrating ones up to the joint of the hip, and up to the knot of the tail.
From that by which is known the penetrating fistula up to the anus, also from the non-penetrating one, it is, that you insert your index finger into the anus: and you insert a subtle probe made of brass or iron into the fistula: when there is no tortuosity.
Which if there is tortuosity in it, then insert into it a subtle probe made of lead, or a hair from the hairs of horses, until you feel the probe, or the hair on your finger.
Which if you do not feel it deeply, nor does anything proceed from the opening from evacuation, nor flatulence, nor worms as I said: then know that it is a non-penetrating one: proceed therefore to the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating up to the bladder or to the passage of urine: then its signification is the exit of urine from it, and prohibition of it by this, that the place be consolidated with medicines.
If it is a penetrating one up to the joint of the hip or to the socket of the hip: then its sign is that the probe penetrates up to that place, if there is no tortuosity in it up to the mouth: and finding pain in the surrounding part, and that pus always exits from it: and that medication is not effective in it, nor is it consolidated with an ointment.
And in all these penetrating fistulas there is no cure at all: and the treatment of them is labor and vanity to him, from foolish medicines, on which it is formed.
In that which is not penetrating and not chronic, healing may be expected with a plaster: according to what I relate to you, and I have already proven: and it is, so that the weak person lies on his back between your hands: and lift his legs up above his hips, and his hips are inclined towards his abdomen. Then a probe of lead or bronze is inserted, if there is a tortuousness in the fistula, until you know where it passes through.
If the weak person feels it around the anus, then it is necessary that you insert your index finger into the anus.
If you feel on your finger that the probe has already penetrated through by itself being detected, besides what you feel between your finger and the sifac, or flesh: then you certainly know that it is penetrating: do not therefore labor in it, since its healing is not, as we have said.
They have said, however, that flesh is healed in certain men and from the medication by which healing is hoped for, it is to apply a subtle cauterium of ignition according to the width of the fistula, as previously described, and insert the ignited thing into the fistula until it reaches around the anus. Then repeat that two or three times, until you know that all those added and filtered-out fleshy growths, which are similar to the quill of a bird's feather, have been burned.
Then treat it with cloths wrapped in butter, until the burned-out flesh comes out: then treat it with ointments that generate and consolidate flesh.
If it is healed, it is good.
And if not, then it does not heal with any other cure.
And if the probe comes out and has not reached up to your finger which is in the anus, and there is between it and the probe a thick covering of flesh or sifac: and you see the fistula in what follows the surface of the skin, then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you dissect with the probe that is in the fistula, until the dissection reaches where the end of the probe meets, and the probe is freed and falls out.
Then clean those filtered flesh parts that resemble a bird's crop or gizzard, so that nothing remains in them.
But if the blood overcomes you and separates between you and your operation so that it cuts off those flesh parts, then it is better to cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine.
For the cauterization with fire brings together good habits, an adjustment of those added flesh parts, and a cutting off of the blood, and a drying of the moistures.
Then treat it with dressings wrapped in butter or pounded cabbage stalks, until the spot emits pus and those flesh parts that were burned protrude in the pus.
Then treat the wound with consolidating ointments that generate hard flesh, and there are medicines in which there are astringency and drying.
For when it is restored, then it is already healed: and do not repeat the treatment.
But if the fistula has already penetrated to the depth of the anus and is prolonged from the surplus of the body, then insert your finger into the anus and examine with it.
If therefore you feel a thin layer, and between you and it there is a covering of sifac or flesh, and it is near to penetration: then the operation is not in that, except by way of trust and hope.
Which is, that one of the three methods is administered in it: either you cauterize it, as we have said: or you cut it, until you achieve its concavity, so that it is possible for you to insert dressings and cure from nearby. And do not proceed much with the cutting, so that you do not injure the membrane that contains the anus, and it happens over the weak point of the passage of excretion without control. Then treat it with what we have said.
For the wound will be healed; either you will lengthen the bandage, and clean it after you cut it up to near the anus, as we have said, or with a probe, or with another instrument of a sharp extremity. Then clean those filtered flesh parts which are in the cut, as far as you can with scrutiny.
Then consider the restoration of the whole wound with the cut, and the upper orifice where it consolidates: and a remaining fistula stays open in the interior part of the anus, and will be lighter on the weaker.
And when a fistula follows in this manner: and it is, when you insert the probe into the Fistula: and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with skin and edge of the anus: then take the probe of perforated extremity, which is like a needle alekef, that is, preparing hides, in this form. And insert into it a thread wound from five threads, and tie around it. Then insert the probe with the thread into the Fistula, until it reaches its concavity.
If then it is penetrating the edge of the anus inside near, then pull out the thread from that hole: so that you insert your finger into the anus, and pull out the end of the thread, and bring together the two ends: and tie both, and leave it for one day, or two days: and as much as the thread cuts into the flesh, tie it well, until the fleshes which are between the two ends of the thread cut and fall: then treat the wound, until it consolidates, and is healed.
If however the orifice of the Fistula does not penetrate: then make it penetrate by whatever method is prepared for you, unless it is deep within. For you should not do that on account of the liver, so as not to cut it.
Then do with it as we have said, until it is healed.
The shape of the spoon for a patient with a fistula, whose curvature is sharp and one part is not sharp, so that it does not cut what is not necessary, as you see.
Chapter 81.
On the suture of hemorrhoids, from which blood flows from the cutting of them: and the cure of fissures.
There are two kinds of hemorrhoids. Either they are inside the anus, like vessels full of blood, or they are like a grain of a nut. And among them there are small and large ones: and blood flows from them always, and there is one, and there are many. And they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
But truly those that are outside the anus, for the most part have little humidity, from which flows watery or yellowish fluid, or a small amount of blood with constant flow: and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of that which is inside the anus, is that you should apply to the weak one so that it may sit: and it is squeezed, until the anus comes out, and the threads appear to you. Therefore hang them with hooks: or hold them with your finger. Then cut them at their roots.
If they are not held by the hooks, because of their humidity and softening: then take them with a coarse cloth, or with a thread from two twisted wool, and pull them out with your fingers. Then cut them, and powder over them after the cutting certain hot powders, so that they may take the place of a cautery. Or cauterize them according to what was previously described in the chapter on cauterizing. Then treat them with the remainder of the treatment until they are healed.
What if the anus does not obey evacuation, then give a weak enema of such a composition that there is a little mordicatio to cause it to loosen what is in the anus and to obey evacuation quickly when the weak one evacuates.
If however the hemorrhoids are external to the anus, then their treatment is easy and simple: and it is that you seize them with your finger or seize them with a hook, and cut them. Then treat them with what we have said, until they are healed.
And he who is averse to cutting with iron, then it is necessary that you administer their suture according to this method. Take an unwound thread and insert it into the needle. Then pull out the hemorrhoid upwards and make it penetrate with the needle at its root from the other side: and tie the two ends of the thread on the lower part of the needle, and let them be crosswise: and constrict the hemorrhoid tightly. Then knot the thread, and pull out the needle.
Do this with all the hemorrhoids, and leave one of them untouched: nor touch itself, so that it runs from it an excess of blood.
Then put on the anus a cloth steeped in rose oil or cerate, and put it on the anus: and order the weak one to rest. Then leave it alone until it falls off.
When therefore the hemorrhoids fall off, treat them with ointments and the remainder of the treatment, until they are healed.
On the treatment of Fissures. For often it happens from the dryness of feces and the constriction of nature.
When therefore they become old and medicine does not penetrate into them: then it is necessary that you rub them with the points of the spatula or with your finger until they become humid and the outer skin which prevents them from consolidating is removed. Then treat them, until they consolidate according to what is suitable.
If they do not consolidate: then treat them again with a more vigorous rubbing than the first, until they bleed much, and then treat them, until they heal.
On the treatment of inverted and not inverted piles, and of rectal fistulas, and of hemorrhoids.
Chapter 82.
Know that a pile is nothing but a round knot according to the color of the body, similar to the head of a nail: and it occurs in the whole body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and toes: and pain happens from them during walking.
It is necessary therefore that what is around the nail be cut, and that it be held with forceps, or with a hook, and that it be eradicated from its root.
Then treat it, and if you want to cauterize it according to what preceded in its chapter.
Of dry hemorrhoids one is a small protrusion, rough, fatty, round on the surface of the body. And they often occur in the hands of children.
And the treatment of it is, that you stretch the hemorrhoid, and cut it: or tie it with a thread of silk: or with a probe, until it falls off. And if you want, cauterize it according to what was previously mentioned with fire, or with sharp medicine: and now both inverted and not inverted hemorrhoids are eradicated with an instrument that I will describe.
A boil is also a small fatty, rough, protrusion on the surface of the body, going deep into the flesh: and when it encounters cold, it feels like the biting of a ant, and it occurs in the whole body: and most often it occurs in the hands.
And the treatment of it is, that you take a small feather from a goose's pen, or a strong vulture's feather: and put that small feather on the boil, until the circle of the feather contains the parts of it. Then turn your hand with the cannula, until you reach what is in the circumference of the anal fistula; and you will put it in the depth of the flesh, and eradicate the fistula from its root.
And if you need to, do that with a cannula of bronze or iron, according to this form.
Let the upper part of the cannula be at the edge, drawing the thread which is wound around it, so that the grasp and rotation of it may be alleviated on the finger.
And if you need to, cauterize the fistula according to what has been mentioned in the cauterization of Athelil in the chapter on cauterization.
Chapter 83.
Of the forms of instruments which are administered for clysters in diseases of the anus, and of purging of the belly, and of colic.
Sometimes the clyster is made of silver, or of gold, or of forged brass, or of hammered metal.
And sometimes they are made small and large from these instruments, according to those for which they are administered.
That therefore which is administered in the treatment of small children should be small: and those whose anuses are weak, or painful, their clysters thus also.
A large clyster.
The cannula of it, that is, the upper head in which the thread is tied, should be wide according to this manner: and it should have a distinction so that the thread can be tied as you see, and its lower end which is inserted into the anus, should be rounded, that is, not open, smooth, gentle, drawing to subtlety: and on one of its sides there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole.
And the width of the hole should be according to the thickness of the threads, and a little thicker, and there should be a thread in which medicines are placed from the bladder of an animal: or from the paper of an egg, which is according to the form of small asafoetida: whose root is one palm.
And it should be perforated with many holes as it is revolving, and let there be a space which is between every hole the thickness of a finger. Then insert into those holes a strong thread made from crude thread, which is of ten threads, or around that, and tie to it a thread like astofara. When therefore the thread is placed in it, let it be tightened at the head of the clisters between two pads with strong constriction. Then inject with it.
And this is the form of the circle and the utensil depicted here, and of the holes.
The quality of injecting with it, is that you fill the thread or bladder with medicine, which is warmed according to the quantity of the tolerance of the weak person: and beware that it not be very hot or very cold.
Then the weak person should breathe again on his back, and lift his thighs up to the top, and put under him a cushion, that is, a skin on which men sit, or a cloth.
Then anoint the extremity of the clister with oil, or with the white of egg, or with the mucus of fenugreek, or similar things. Then insert it into the anus with ease. Then the servant should take the thread with both his hands at the same time, and press it out with vehemence, until he evacuates all that is in the clister into the intestine.
Then extract the clister, and let the weak person lift his thighs to his side.
Which if the medicine brings it to the end, then let him hold as much as he can. And if he sleeps with it the whole night, it is the more ultimate in juvament.
If however you inject him with the enemas of the belly during illnesses and its exit is hastened: then repeat the clister until he is cured.
What if there are hemorrhoids in the anus, or painful apostemes, then let it be a subtle and mild suppository, from those suppositories with which children are treated.
And this is the form of a subtle suppository on which the skin is stretched tight.
Head 83.
Already I have spoken in the division of the cure of wounds what was suitable for the book, and I will say here the cure of them with the hand, and with medicines according to completion.
I say therefore, that wounds are distinguished according to that by which they are made into wounds, and according to the place on which the wound falls.
The things by which wounds are often made are like the throwing of a stone: or the cutting of a sword, or of a knife: or the striking with a lance, or with wood, or with an arrow: and similar to these from many things.
The wounds which are made according to the places of the body are, such as a wound that falls on the head, or neck, or chest, or belly, or liver: and similar from these members.
And I will describe the cures of certain wounds, so that I may set down that reasoning and rule concerning the remaining wounds.
And I will begin with simple head wounds: since the recollection of compounders will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
I say therefore. When there is a simple wound in the head and it is not a fracture of bone: consider then if it is from the throwing of a stone, or similar things, and has already broken the skin to such an extent: and it is a large wound, and often above the weak event of a hot aposteme: then perform promptly phlebotomy of the head at once: and do not delay it: and let out for it from the blood according to the quantity of its virtue: if there is nothing that prohibits phlebotomy, especially if the blood which comes out of the wound is little. And let bloodletting be from the opposite side of the wounded part.
And let bloodletting be from the opposite side of the wounded part. And let the weak man beware for himself of overeating, and wine, and coarse foods.
If something prohibits diminishment, then he will diminish from food, and not approach flesh, nor wine.
And put on the wound if there happens to it a hot aposteme, a plaster underneath in rose oil alone, or with wine in which there is astringency.
If you are secure from a hot aposteme, then put on the wound, if it is recent with its own blood, and the air has not changed it, a powder which I will describe after a little while: and if the air has already changed it, then put on it certain ointments, until it be healed.
If the wound is large, or is from a cut of a sword, and similar things: and its lips do not come together by themselves with pus, then bring them together with a suture, according to what I will describe in wounds of the abdomen concerning their suture.
If the wound has already been torn from the bone, and is hanging, and there is no retention of it, except in a small sling: then cut it. Then treat the wound with medicines, and restore to it hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the weak person, that he be nourished with foods in which there is thickness, such as are heads and cooked wheat, until it be like a pulse: and similar things.
What if you find in the skin rot, and it does not adhere to the bone: then cut away the whole rotten part, and cast it away: then treat that.
If however in these wounds there is an artery, or a vein from which blood flows: and it is not stopped by medicines, then tie above the artery. If therefore you find it not cut, then cut it with a spatula, or tie it. What if necessity demands it when it does not conjoin what we have said, then cauterize it, until blood is let.
If however these wounds are small, simple, then their treatment is easy, slight: so that you powder over them this powder: because it consolidates them before it changes them to air.
Method of the Powder for Incorporation. Take one part of olibanum and two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unslaked lime: pound all together much, and sift: and fill the wound with it, and bind with a good bandage, until it adheres well to it, and coagulates with the blood.
Then bind it above with cloths, and leave it, nor loosen it while it remains, so that it does not become an aposteme. For the medicine should not be eradicated from it until it is healed.
And when it is made with lime alone, when you do not have olibanum and dragon's blood present, the latter also performs the same operation in many large wounds, when it is suitable to be placed on them and bound, and they are recent wounds with their own blood, which the air has not altered.
What if the air has already altered them by some alteration, especially when it is in the summer season, then it is not in a position for the intention of this powder: therefore treat it with what we have said, so that you place on them certain digestive ointments: or place on them poultices made from barley flour, made with water and honey, until they emit pus. Then treat the remaining ones with a cure, until they are healed.
If it happens with a wound and a fracture of the bone, and it is small, then extract it with a gesture: and I will now speak of the cure of fractures of the head in what is to come.
On neck wounds.
If a wound occurs on the neck, then there is no difference between it and a head wound as regards treatment when it is simple.
If the nerve or artery of the neck has already been cut, then if it is a nerve, there is no ingenuity except that treatment for it should be done with what causes violent constriction, such as ziniar and zegi and similar things. For they injure the nerves and constrict them.
And you should not apply anything cold to the wound at all, since the substance of the nerves is cold and its continuity is with the brain, which is the most elevated of the organs: and let that by which it may be treated be from gentle medicines, such as lotus paste with sweet water infused several times with oil, or with rose oil and tuthia when it has also been washed with sweet water: and other mineral stones, in this manner, and moist ointments.
If the wound is large, then administer a suture: or constrict its lips with poultices. Then treat it until it heals.
If the wound has depth, or a sinus occurs in its lower part in which pus has already collected, then pierce it in the most depressed place.
If an artery has been cut in the wound and a flow of its blood has followed, then separate it, or cut it off, and ligate it: or cauterize it if necessity demands it.
If the spongy part of the throat has been cut, or the whole of it, and the alhaudegi have been saved: then bring together the lips of the skin with a suture over a cane in the throat, and do not touch the throat, but reduce it to its natural shape. Then tie it tightly with a bandage and loosen it after a few days. Then treat it with ointments in which there is astringency and excitation, until it heals.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then perforate it: then if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all of them, or as many as you can: and what is not prepared, leave it, until the wound putrefies and is separated and the protrusion is alleviated.
What if the wound is fresh, then powder over it the powder that I have described. If however a bone is seen in the wound and a fistula forms: then treat it with that which I will mention in its own chapter.
On the wound of the shoulder blade.
If it is a thrust of a lance or a knife: and you see its depth, then consider it. If therefore a gurgling sound comes out of the wound, when the weak person breathes from it, then know that the wound is mortal.
What if the depth is not to it, and it is fresh with its blood: then do not put on it powder from the first hour, nor tie it, so that the blood is not retained in its depth, and returned to the heart, and kills the weak person: but put on it an attracting ointment, and loosen it twice a day.
If indeed the ointment is not present to you, then put in the mouth of the wound old cloth, so that it sucks up what comes out from it of humidities: and make that the weak person sleeps on the wound, so that what accumulates in it runs.
If indeed the wound has already passed three days, or more, and no spasms have happened to the weak person, nor bad heart tremors, nor constriction in breathing, and you see the rest of its dispositions good: then know that the wound is safe. Treatment is thus applied to it with bandages, and the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
If the healing of the ulcer is excavated and it always opens, then you should know that a fistula has already been formed. Treatment is thus applied to it from its own source.
And if the wound is from a cut of a sword or a knife, and it is simple on the surface of the breast or the back: then treat it with what has preceded concerning suture, if it is large: or with powder, if it is small.
If however it has already made an impression on the bone, and a fragment has been cut from it: then probe the wound, and hasten to extract those fragments, if they are separated. If indeed they are not separated, then leave them, until the wound becomes putrid, for the extraction of them will be alleviated.
The judgment of treatment for wounds occurring in other limbs is the same as what we have already said.
On the wounds of the abdomen, and the protrusion of the intestines, and their extrusion.
The disruption that occurs to the abdomen is great, moderate, and small.
From a great one, it happens that the intestine or many of the intestines protrude.
For which reason the insertion and suture of them is more violent and difficult.
And a small disruption also becomes difficult in another way. It follows therefore, that the reduction of them is more difficult, if you do not hasten to insert them in their place immediately: because they become inflated, open, and enlarged: for which reason their re-entry becomes difficult.
On account of this therefore, a moderate disruption is better than the others: because with it the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is with these two types.
Know that the suture of a vein is secondary to four methods.
Two common suture methods come together in the suture of a vein, and in the suture of other wounds of the body; and two other suture methods properly communicate with the remaining wounds. However, they are more proper for the suture of a vein: and I will describe to you each one with exposition, and declaration.
I say therefore, that when a wound is small, and something exits from it from the intestine, and it becomes difficult to reduce it: then it is suitable for one of the two methods. Either because of the smallness of the disruption, as we have said: or because there is inflammation in the intestine on account of cold air.
When therefore it is thus, then it is necessary that you warm it, so that you immerse a sponge, or a moist cloth in lukewarm water alone. Or you boil in water the juice of cypress, and cumin, and spike, and chamomile, and apply it to the intestine, until the inflammation is resolved.
Sometimes make a wine in which there is astringency: and it is better than water alone for resolving the inflammation.
When therefore you see that the inflammation has already been resolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which marshmallow or mallow has been boiled. For by that the entrance of it is alleviated with something little.
If however its return is excavated after this cure, then make a small incision in the disruption, with an instrument with which hemorrhoids are cut.
And the first cure is better when it is prepared, than the incision: and there is no need to cut after necessity and lack of the instrument.
Let one part of it be twisted and sharp, and the other part not sharp, and the extremity not be with the subtlety of a spatula, but rather more blunt for a little while: and it is that which resembles a reed, as you see.
When a wound is enlarged, and the intestine protrudes, then it is necessary that there be a reduction of it according to its natural form in its own proper place, if possible, over that, because it is better.
When the disruption is large in the lower part of the abdomen, then it is necessary that you make the weak one lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head. And if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, then put its head, and its chest higher than its lower parts.
And similarly if there is a disruption in one of the two parts of the abdomen, then put your intention and your consideration always in this, that the part in which there is a wound be higher than the other part.
And so it is necessary that you administer it in great wounds and in medium wounds.
In small wounds, put it according to what is prepared for you.
Then make that the assistant, a pious minister, who holds the whole disruption in their hand, be present between your hands, and bring together its lips. Then let him who follows, apply to it a suture, something after something, and this is the common method of one suture.
And it is that you take a needle, or a number of needles according to the quantity of the wound's depth. Then measure from the edge of the disruption a quantity of a finger's width, that is, of the doctor, and insert one needle beyond which you will insert thread in the two edges of the skin, with the two edges of the suture, which is under the skin from the interior, until you make it penetrate from the other side, and you have now brought together two edges of the skin, and two edges of the suture: and they become four stitches.
Then tie with doubled thread around the needle several times on both sides at once, until the two lips of the wound are brought together by a proper joining.
Then diminish the thickness of the digit also, and fix a second needle in it: afterwards tie it with thread, just as you did with the first needle. Do not cease to do that with what you insert from the needles, until you complete the constriction of the whole wound.
And let the needles be medium between thickness and fineness: for thin needles easily pierce the flesh: and thick ones are difficult to enter the skin: because of that it is necessary that they be medium in fineness and thickness.
And it is not necessary that the needle be fixed in two extremes of the skin that are close together: so that the flesh is not quickly pierced, and the wound is opened before its own consolidation, and they do not also become elongated with the suture, so that the wound is not prevented from consolidation.
